Commonwealth v. Wright


64 W.D. Appeal Dkt. 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


560 Pa. 34; 742 A.2d 661; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3774


March 9, 1999, Argued  
December 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 1096PGH97 on April 30, 1998, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, at Nos. 387OC & 3871C 1995 on March 27, 1997. Judges: CCP - Pezze, J.; SUPERIOR - Kelly, Joyce, Olszewski, JJ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Superior Court, affirming the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's motion to suppress the firearms seized from his residence, claiming that the police should have obtained a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant shot and injured his wife at his home. Police arrived, arrested appellant, and removed the wife and son. Having obtained neither a search warrant nor consent, troopers searched the residence. Prior to trial, appellant unsuccessfully moved to suppress the firearms seized, and appellant was convicted. The Superior Court affirmed, reasoning that the search was justified pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2711(b), which requires the police to seize weapons used in the commission of certain enumerated offenses, and that the search was also proper due to exigent circumstances. The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania reversed, holding that seizure pursuant to § 2711(b) is subject to limitations of U.S. Const. amend. IV. The statute did not authorize warrantless searches whenever a weapon is implicated in a domestic violence case. Further, no exigent circumstances existed, because no danger would have resulted in the delay occasioned by obtaining a warrant.


OUTCOME: Order of the Superior Court reversed, and case remanded for a new trial. The statute which requires police to seize weapons used in the commission of offenses involving domestic violence did not authorize warrantless search. A seizure under the statute is subject to constitutional limitations.

 

2 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gindlesperger


No. 40 W.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


560 Pa. 222; 743 A.2d 898; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3769


March 9, 1999, Argued  
December 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied June 18, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 4532.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered December 24, 1997, at No. 85PGH97, vacating the Judgment of Sentence and Motion to Suppress is reversed from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, entered February 14, 1996, at No. 1515 of 1994. 706 A.2d 1216 (Pa. Super. 1997). Judges: CCP - Connelly, J.; SUPERIOR - Kelly, Cercone, PJE., Brosky, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth appealed an order from the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which determined that the warrantless use of the WASP device to scan appellee's residence constituted an unlawful search for purposes of U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Police officers entered appellee's basement pursuant to a search warrant and seized marijuana plants. Probable cause for the search was based, in part, on information provided by a confidential informant. Further verification of this tip occurred when a member of the Army National Guard Drug Force, along with local law enforcement, "viewed" appellee's residence using a thermal imaging device known as a "WASP." Subsequently, a search warrant was issued for appellee's home based, in part, on the fact that the detected heat source was consistent with the heat source coming from the artificial lighting used in the growing of marijuana. Appellee was convicted based on this evidence, and appealed. The court held that law enforcement agents' use of an infrared thermal imaging device to scan appellee's private residence without obtaining a search warrant constituted an unlawful search in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; law enforcement agents' use of an infrared thermal imaging device to scan appellee's private residence without first obtaining a search warrant constituted an unlawful search in violation of the Fourth Amendment.

 

3 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Wertz v. Chapman Twp.


No. 134 M.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


559 Pa. 630; 741 A.2d 1272; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3750; 81 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 915; 79 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P40,354


April 26, 1999, Argued  
December 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered February 20, 1998, at 148 C.D. 1997, affirming in part and vacating in part the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Clinton County entered April 12, 1995, at 793-94. 709 A.2d 428 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1998). Judges: Com. Court - Flaherty, Leadbetter, JJ and Silvestri, S.J. /CCP - Hon. Richard M. Saxton.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from an Order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which held that in her action seeking monetary damages under the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act, 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 951-962.2 was not entitled to a trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought employment discrimination suit against township and its supervisors. After her federal claims were dismissed as time-barred, she proceeded under the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act (PHRA), 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 951-962.2. The Pennsylvania Supreme Court found that the general assembly's use of the term "court" in the statute was significant. The court held that simply because the PHRA allowed for legal relief did not translate into a legislative intent to provide for a jury trial. The court ruled that jury trials were constitutionally required only where a jury trial for the claim would have been available when the Pennsylvania constitution was adopted. Having determined that no cause of action for sexual discrimination existed at the time of the adoption of the Pennsylvania constitution, the court determined that plaintiff had no right to a jury trial under the PHRA.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed holding plaintiff was not entitled to a jury trial for claims arising under the Pennsylvania Human Relations Act because the legislature intended judges and not juries to hear claims of discrimination.

 

4 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Stevens


No. 0229 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


559 Pa. 171; 739 A.2d 507; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3227


December 29, 1998, Submitted  
October 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Stevens, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3861 (Pa., Dec. 30, 1999)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Stevens v. Horn, 319 F. Supp. 2d 592, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27534 (W.D. Pa., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County Dated April 29, 1998 at No. 356A of 1992. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. Robert E. Kunselman.
Stevens v. Pennsylvania, 519 U.S. 855, 136 L. Ed. 2d 96, 117 S. Ct. 151, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 5293 (1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County (Pennsylvania) denying petition for review, contending that trial counsel should have conducted additional investigation on mental health issues, and second that the proportionality review violated appellant's constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The court held that because mentally ill defense can not be raised during the guilt phase, appellant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to pursue this defense. The court found that appellant had not proven that presentation of expert testimony concerning appellant's psychosis would have successfully prevented appellee commonwealth from proving appellant's premeditation beyond a reasonable doubt, because the lower court would not have accepted appellant's defense in light of the other evidence that established appellant's premeditation. The court rejected appellant's challenge to the selection of additional prospective jurors by issuing summonses to people at the mall, because appellant could not establish that the method of selection prejudiced him. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding of the aggravating factor of torture because of the number and placement of shots into the victim's body. The court upheld the constitutionality of the proportionality review.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because expert testimony of psychosis would not have prevented appellee from proving premeditation due to other evidence which established appellant's premeditation, and thus counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the issue.

 

5 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Wilson Partners, L.P. v. Board of Fin. & Revenue


48 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 1999, 49 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 1999


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


558 Pa. 462; 737 A.2d 1215; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2975


July 12, 1999, Submitted  
October 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1102.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on February 26, 1999 at Nos. 355 F.R. 1996.

Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered on February 26, 1999 at Nos. 356 F.R. 1996. Judges: Colins, P.J., Doyle, McGinley, Smith, Pellegrini, Kelley, Flaherty, JJ., Commonwealth Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants appealed from the order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), presenting constitutional challenges to the imposition of a tax at the one-percent rate established by the Pennsylvania Realty Transfer Tax Act within the context of a real estate transfer in which one party to the transaction is exempt.


OVERVIEW: Appellants presented constitutional challenges to the imposition of a tax established by the Pennsylvania Realty Transfer Tax Act, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 8101-C to 81134-C, (Act) within the context of a real estate transfer in which one party to the transaction is exempt. Appellants maintained that the Act discriminated against parties dealing with the federal government in violation of the federal supremacy clause, U.S. Const. art. VI, § 2, and that the asserted unequal burden imposed resulted in a violation of principles of uniformity and equal protection. On appeal, the court found that while parties dealing with the federal government encountered a degree of differential treatment in terms of the incidence of taxation under the Act, this difference was without constitutional import, since the economic burden which they bear was deemed to be equivalent. Thus, the taxing scheme under the Act was grounded in a rational basis, as it functioned in a non-discriminatory manner.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the taxing scheme under the Pennsylvania Realty Transfer Tax Act was grounded in a rational basis, as it functioned in a non-discriminatory manner.

Commonwealth v. Koehler


No. 214 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


558 Pa. 334; 737 A.2d 225; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2617


November 16, 1998, Argued  
September 2, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5220. Application for Reargument Denied October 27, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3210.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Koehler, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3210 (Pa., Oct. 27, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Koehler v. Pennsylvania, 531 U.S. 829, 121 S. Ct. 79, 148 L. Ed. 2d 41, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5220 (2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Koehler, 614 Pa. 159, 36 A.3d 121, 2012 Pa. LEXIS 147 (2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Koehler v. Wetzel, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 63118 (M.D. Pa., May 14, 2015)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Koehler, 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2497 (Pa., Nov. 2, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County.
Commonwealth v. Koehler, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2493 (Pa., Aug. 20, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the judgment of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Bradford County (Pennsylvania) that sentenced appellant to death following two convictions for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The court found that evidence presented at appellant's trial, viewed in the light most favorable to the Commonwealth, clearly established sufficient evidence to support both of appellant's convictions for first-degree murder. The testimony of the witnesses, coupled with the forensic evidence, was sufficient for the jury to conclude that the victims were unlawfully killed, that appellant was legally accountable for the conduct of the man who committed the killings, and that appellant had the specific intent to kill and the killings were done with deliberation. The court reviewed the record concluded that the sentences imposed were not the product of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, and that the sentences imposed were not disproportionate to those imposed in similar cases. Further, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the aggravating circumstances found in the murders, and affirmed the verdicts and the sentences of death.


OUTCOME: Judgement affirmed; holding that the death sentences imposed were not the product of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor and that the sentences imposed were not disproportionate to those imposed in similar cases. Evidence was sufficient to support the aggravating circumstances found in the murders.

Commonwealth v. Fahy


No. 215 Capital Appeal Dkt.


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


558 Pa. 313; 737 A.2d 214; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2578


April 15, 1999, Submitted  
August 27, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3004.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Fahy, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3004 (Pa., Oct. 4, 1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Fahy, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 2051 (Pa., Nov. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, at Nos. 2284-2289 February Term 1981, dated December 29, 1997.

Appeal from the Order of the Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, at Nos. 2284-2289, dated December 19, 1997. Judges: C.C.P. - Honorable Alfred F. Sabo.
Commonwealth v. Fahy, 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2568 (Pa., Dec. 2, 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from an order of the Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's request for relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9541, et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to death. Appellant filed a petition for collateral review under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9541 et seq., and the petition was dismissed. Appellant twice filed a petition for stay of execution, which the PCRA court denied both times. Appellant then petitioned the PCRA court to allow him to waive all collateral proceedings and to withdraw all appeals so that his death sentence could be carried out. Appellant's request was granted. Appellant was colloquied regarding his understanding of the waiver of his rights, and the PCRA court concluded that appellant was competent to waive his right to collateral review and appellate proceedings. Defense counsel's appeals on behalf of appellant were denied. On final appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellant's petition was properly dismissed as untimely, and that the court had no jurisdiction to review the merits of his petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that appellant's petition was properly dismissed as untimely, and that the court had no jurisdiction to review the merits of his petition.

Commonwealth v. Hill


No. 32 E.D. Appeal Docket 1998, No. 104 M.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


558 Pa. 238; 736 A.2d 578; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2381


February 3, 1999, Argued  
August 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, dated July 29, 1997, at No. 1740 Philadelphia 1996, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, dated April 23, 1996, at Nos. 1749-53. Judges: CCP - Hon. Jane Cutler Greenspan / SUPERIOR - McEwen, P.J., Hoffman, J., Cercone, P.J.E.

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, dated August 27, 1996, at No. 2953 Philadelphia 1995, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County, dated November 15, 1995, at No. 92CR589. Judges: CCP - Hon. Jay W. Myers / Sueprior Court - Kelly, Johnson and Olszewski, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two consolidated criminal cases, appellants sought review from the order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) that affirmed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County. Both appellants alleged the trial court erred by denying their motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidated appeal, appellants alleged that the superior court erred by affirming the trial court's denial of their motions to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed. Under Pa. R. Crim. P. 1100, appellants were entitled to have their charges dismissed if they were not brought to trial within 365 days of the filing of the criminal complaint. Since the superior court's error only resulted in the improper exclusion of a four-day period for one appellant, that appellant failed to establish that his trial was held beyond the 365-day deadline. Therefore, he was not entitled to a dismissal. As to second appellant, the Commonwealth was duly diligent in prosecuting appellant and that the delay in starting trial was occasioned by circumstances beyond the control of the Commonwealth. Therefore, second appellant was not entitled to have the charges against him dismissed.


OUTCOME: Affirmed. Where the court's error only resulted in exclusion of four-day period, appellant failed to prove trial was held beyond 365-day deadline; appellant was diligently prosecuted and trial's delay was beyond prosecutor's control.

 

9 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. McCurdy


No. 35 W.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


558 Pa. 65; 735 A.2d 681; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2230


September 17, 1998, Argued  
August 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania, No. 1385 PGH, 1996, dated May 9, 1997, reversing in part and affirming in part the Judgment of Sentence entered June 24, 1996 in the Court of Common Pleas of Indiana County, Criminal Division at No. 786 Crim. 1995. JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Honorable William J. Martin / SUPERIOR - Popovich, Johnson, CERCONE, PJE, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pennsylvania reversing in part and affirming in part his sentence. Appellant was convicted of DUI, homicide by vehicle while DUI, and involuntary manslaughter. Appellant contended that because his conviction under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(5) was reversed, his convictions under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(1) and homicide by vehicle while DUI must also have been reversed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the order affirming in part and reversing in part his sentence after conviction of DUI, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(1), (4), and (5); homicide by vehicle while DUI, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3735; homicide by vehicle, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732; and involuntary manslaughter, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2504. Appellant contended because his § 3731(a)(5) conviction was reversed due to a constitutional infirmity, his convictions under § 3731(a)(1) and homicide by vehicle must also have been reversed. Appellant contended he was entitled to a new trial. Appellant also alleged that the jury was improperly instructed that evidence of his blood alcohol level could be considered in evaluating proof pursuant to § 3731(a)(1). The court disagreed, holding that homicide by vehicle while DUI required a conviction for DUI pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731and proof that the violation caused the death. Once established, the unconstitutionality of an alternate method of proof under § 3731(a)(5) did not negate proof supportive of § 3721(a)(1), particularly when the blood alcohol level was otherwise admissible under § 3721a)(1).


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions and sentences for DUI, homicide by vehicle, and involuntary manslaughter were affirmed. The unconstitutionality of an alternative method of proof did not negate the proof supportive of conviction, particularly when appellant's blood alcohol level was otherwise admissible.

 

10 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Petroll


179 M.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


558 Pa. 565; 738 A.2d 993; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2099


April 30, 1998, Argued  
July 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Harsh v. Petroll, 840 A.2d 404, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 911 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered June 18, 1997 at No. 2429PHL96 affirming the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County entered June 28, 1996 at No. 2616 of 1995. JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Hon Lawrence F. Stengel/ SUPERIOR - POPOVICH, JOHNSON, JJ., CERCONE, P.J.E.
Commonwealth v. Petroll, 696 A.2d 817, 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1611 (Pa. Super. Ct., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from order of Superior Court affirming judgment of Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), finding appellant guilty of homicide by vehicle, failing to drive at safe speed, and careless driving. Appellant argued warrantless searches and subsequent seizures violate Penn. Const. art. I, §8 and U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver appealed his conviction for homicide by vehicle, failing to drive at safe speed, and careless driving, claiming that because police lacked probable cause, and no exception to the warrant requirement applied, their warrantless searches and seizures of items from his tractor-trailer were unconstitutional. The court found warrantless seizure of the radar detector was permissible under the plain view doctrine. Further, Pennsylvania had a substantial interest in regulating the trucking industry for public safety, but 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. 6308(b) did not authorize an administrative search without a warrant for the items seized in this case; it did not give police unlimited discretion to search a vehicle for evidence of a crime. The closely regulated business exception to the warrant requirement did not apply. The error was harmless, however, because evidence of guilt was so overwhelming that jury would have found appellant guilty even without improperly admitted evidence.


OUTCOME: Affirmed because administrative search without warrant for items seized in this case was improper; police did not have unlimited discretion to search commercial vehicle after accident for evidence of crime; error was harmless.

 

11 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Scavello


No. 168 Middle District Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


557 Pa. 429; 734 A.2d 386; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1892


April 27, 1999, Argued  
July 2, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Superior Court entered October 15, 1997 at No. 542PHL96 reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, entered January 17, 1996 at No. 0576-94. 703 A.2d 36 (Pa. Super, 1997). Judges: Superior Court - Cirrilo, Cercone, P.J.E., Montemuro, S.J. / CCP - Hon. William T. Nicholas, P.J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which reversed the lower court's denial of appellee driver's motion to suppress and held that an officer's stop of appellee driver was illegal because appellee driver's attempt to avoid a police roadblock did not give rise to reasonable suspicion that he was violating the law.


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver was driving toward a roadblock and made a legal u-turn to avoid it. An officer followed appellee and stopped him not far from the roadblock. Appellee was arrested after he failed a field sobriety test and was later convicted of underage drinking and driving under the influence of alcohol. Appellee moved to suppress the evidence obtained as a result of the stop, claiming that the police had no reasonable suspicion to justify the stop. The motion was denied, but on appeal the lower appellate court reversed, holding that appellee's attempt to avoid the roadblock did not give rise to a reasonable suspicion of criminal conduct that would justify the stop. Appellant state sought review of the order, contending that the officer was authorized to stop the vehicle because he was engaged in checking vehicles at the roadblock and that avoidance of the roadblock was sufficient justification for the stop. The court held that a vehicle stop at a location away from the roadblock could only be made if the officer had reasonable grounds to suspect a violation and that avoidance of the roadblock alone was not sufficient. The lower appellate court's order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower appellate court's order reversing the suppression ruling, finding that appellee driver's avoidance of the roadblock did not provide a basis for a vehicle stop because there is no requirement that a driver go through a roadblock and the officer did not have a reasonable suspicion that the vehicle was involved in criminal conduct.

 

12 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Williams


No. 84 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997, No. 14 W.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


557 Pa. 285; 733 A.2d 593; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1878; 78 A.L.R.5th 731


September 16, 1998, Argued  
June 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 1, 1999. Certiorari Denied January 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 146.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, at No. 922 of 1997 entered September 23, 1997.

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court at No. 2466PGH97 entered 3/9/98 transferring case to Supreme Court from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, entered October 1, 1997 at No. 900 of 1997.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant state sought review of the order of the Erie County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania), granting the appellee's motion for extraordinary relief. The appellee challenged the constitutionality of the sexually violent predator provisions of Pennsylvania's Megan's Law, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791-9799.6.


OVERVIEW: The appellee was convicted of two counts of involuntary deviate sexual intercourse, two counts of indecent assault, and one count of corruption of minors after he allegedly had sexual contact with a nine-year old boy. The appellee was sentenced to an aggregate sentence of more than ten years incarceration and ordered to be evaluated as a sexually violent predator under Pennsylvania Megan's Law (the Act), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791-9799.6), a statute requiring the registration of sex offenders. The appellee challenged the constitutionality of the sexually violent predator provisions of the Act. The court found that the Act had inadequate due process protection for individuals being evaluated as sexually violent predators. The court determined that the burden of proving an individual to be a sexually violent predator should rest with the prosecution, and not require the individual to attempt to rebut the presumption of his classification as a sexually violent predator. The court therefore struck the sexually violent predator provisions of the Act and remanded to the trial court for disposition of the remainder of the issues on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court found all the provisions pertaining to sexually violent predators to be violative of the procedural due process guarantees of the Constitution. The matter was remanded to the trial court for disposition of all remaining issues on appeal.

In re T.R.


No. 89 E.D. Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


557 Pa. 99; 731 A.2d 1276; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1798


April 30, 1997, Argued  
June 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered October 5, 1995 at No. 3682PHL94 affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Family Division, entered September 29, 1994 At Nos. 9204-6912, 9405-2358, 2359 & 2360.



DISPOSITION: The order of Superior Court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the Order of the Superior Court Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order that appellant undergo a psychiatric examination to determine whether appellant was able to care for her children.


OVERVIEW: Children were removed from home of appellant mother after injuries went unexplained. After the trial court affirmed an order that appellant undergo a psychiatric examination to determine whether appellant was able to care for her children, appellant sought review. On appeal, the issue was whether a court which adjudicated a juvenile dependency matter could order a parent to undergo psychological evaluation and disclose the results of the evaluation to interested parties. The court reversed the order requiring appellant to undergo a psychiatric examination because the trial court elevated the interests of the state beyond all reasonable limits and the court concluded that there was no governmental interest sufficient to negate the mother's assertion of her right of privacy. The court disagreed with the trial court's conclusion that less intrusive means were not available.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order requiring appellant to undergo a psychiatric examination because the trial court elevated the interests of the state beyond all reasonable limits and the court concluded that there was no governmental interest sufficient to negate the mother's assertion of her right of privacy.

 

14 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Ppg Indus. v. Bd. of Fin. & Revenue


No. 87 M.D. Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


567 Pa. 565; 790 A.2d 252; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1734


September 16, 1997, Argued  
June 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated June 19, 1996, at No. 2355 C.D. 1987, affirming the Order of the Board of Finance and Revenue dated October 2, 1987, at No. R-10-904 681 A.2d 832 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1996).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania corporation sought review of an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) affirming an order of appellee board of finance and revenue holding that appellant was not entitled to a manufacturing exemption for value of property and payroll for manufacturing activities outside of appellant's Pennsylvania headquarters, pursuant to 72 Penn. Stat. § 7602(a). Appellant asserted the tax was unconstitutionally discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Pennsylvania corporation conducted manufacturing operations in Pennsylvania and other states. Appellant was required to pay a capital stock tax on its Pennsylvania headquarters, pursuant to 72 Penn. Stat. § 7602(a). Appellant calculated its capital stock tax as if it were a foreign corporation paying a franchise tax and entitled to manufacturing exemptions, pursuant to 72 Penn. Stat. § 7602(b)(1). After auditing appellant's 1983 tax return, the department of revenue held that appellant was not entitled to the manufacturing exemption as calculated. Appellant sought review of the resettlement, and appellee board of finance and revenue affirmed the recalculation. Appellant filed a petition for review, challenging appellee's order on constitutional and statutory construction grounds, which was denied and affirmed. Appellant filed a direct appeal. The court reversed judgment in favor of appellant and remanded the case for further proceedings because the manufacturing exemption to Pennsylvania's capital stock tax facially discriminated against interstate commerce and afforded preferential treatment to corporations engaged in manufacturing activities in Pennsylvania.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of appellant Pennsylvania corporation in suit challenging appellee board of finance and revenue's decision that appellant was not entitled to a manufacturing exemption under its capital stock tax for property and payroll activities outside Pennsylvania, because the manufacturing exemption to Pennsylvania's capital stock tax facially discriminated against interstate commerce.

 

15 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Denbow v. Borough of Leetsdale


7 W.D. Appeal Dkt. 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 567; 729 A.2d 1113; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1594; 139 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,707


September 14, 1998, Argued  
June 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania entered August 20, 1997 at No. 2867 C.D. 1996 affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, Pennsylvania entered October 15, 1996 at No. GD94-1993.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Commonwealth Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers sought review of an order of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania entering judgment for appellee borough in breach of contract action filed against appellee. Appellants' breach of contract action contested appellee's repudiation of pay increases in an addenda to a collective bargaining agreement. Appellants asserted that Pa. Const. art. III, § 26 prohibiting pay increases did not apply to local municipalities.


OVERVIEW: Appellee borough council entered into a collective bargaining agreement with the borough's police officers, which included terms on wages. The agreement did not include a wage re-opener provision. After two council members were not re-elected, appellee approved an addendum to the agreement giving police officers substantial pay increases. When appellee was reorganized, it repudiated the addenda to the agreement. Appellant police officers filed a breach of contract action against appellee. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee. Appellant sought review on the issue of whether Pa. Const. art. III, § 26 operated to prohibit a municipality from granting raises to municipal employees who were already covered by an employment contract. The court affirmed judgment for appellee and held that pursuant to Pa. Const. art. III, § 26, municipalities, being creatures of the sovereign, were constrained just like the general assembly from allocating extra compensation to public employees already covered by a contract of employment. The court held that municipal corporations had no inherent powers and could do only those things that the legislature authorized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment for appellee borough in breach of contract action filed by appellant police officers based upon appellee's repudiation of an addendum to a collective bargaining agreement allowing pay increases, and held that pursuant to Pa. Const. art. III, § 26, municipalities, being creatures of the sovereign, were constrained from allocating extra compensation to public employees already covered by a contract of employment.

 

16 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Williams


No. 193 Capital Appeal Dkt.


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


557 Pa. 207; 732 A.2d 1167; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1552


July 21, 1998, Submitted  
June 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Commonwealth v. Williams, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 710 (Pa., Apr. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County entered on March 31, 1997 at CC Nos. 9101-2457, 2458, 2459 & 2460 denying Petition for Relief under the Post-Conviction Relief Act. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. John J. Poserina, Jr.
Williams v. Pennsylvania, 516 U.S. 1051, 133 L. Ed. 2d 671, 116 S. Ct. 717, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 135 (1996)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the PCRA court is affirmed. The matter is remanded for limited further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), denying post-conviction relief in his capital case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Following the affirmance of the conviction and sentence on direct appeal, defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief. In denying the petition, the lower court restated the procedural history and, without further explanation, adopted the state's brief. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, holding that post-conviction relief was not available to the extent that appellant had asserted general claims of trial error that were not preserved at trial and raised on direct appeal. The court, however, reversed in part and remanded with directions for the lower court to render its own, independent findings of fact and conclusions of law concerning certain claims, including allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court explained that that the independent role of the judiciary was not served by the wholesale adoption of the state's brief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, finding that post-conviction relief was not available on appellant's claims of trial error that were not preserved at trial and raised on direct appeal. The court reversed in part and remanded for limited further proceedings, concluding that claims, which included the adequacy of representation, required the lower court to render independent findings, rather than the adoption of the state's brief.

 

17 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Allen


No. 33 W.D. Appeal Dkt. 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


557 Pa. 135; 732 A.2d 582; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1603


September 8, 1997, Submitted  
May 25, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Superior Court at No. 1972PGH95 entered December 16, 1996 affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered October 16, 1995 at Nos. CC 85-00182, CC 85-00183, CC 85-00184, CC 85-00185, CC 85-00186, CC-85-00187, CC-85-00188, CC 85-00315.

JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Honorable Robert E. Dauer, P.J. / SUPERIOR - Cavanaugh, Johnson, Cercone, P.J.E., JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order rendered by the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) that denied appellant's post conviction relief petition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with eight counts of burglary and two counts of receiving stolen property. He pled guilty to all counts and was sentenced to consecutive sentences for a total of 80 years imprisonment. After several proceedings, appellant filed an amended pro se petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9551, alleging that trial counsel was ineffective for leading him to believe that that his sentence would be shorter. The court denied the petition. The Superior Court affirmed. Appellant filed a second PCRA petition alleging that his guilty plea was unlawful because he was not advised that he could be subject to consecutive sentences. The Court sought to determine whether a "miscarriage of justice" occurred which would warrant relief on a repetitive PCRA petition, where the record failed to reflect that defendant was made aware of the possibility of consecutive sentences. The court affirmed the order denying post conviction relief. There was not a miscarriage of justice where the record reflected that appellant was aware that he could get consecutive sentences and where appellant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellant's post conviction relief petition because the heavy burden of proof for an ineffective assistance of counsel claim in the context of a repetitive post conviction relief petition precluded the finding of a miscarriage of justice.

Commonwealth v. Cox


No. 109 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 368; 728 A.2d 923; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1263


January 28, 1997, Argued  
May 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied July 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2190. Certiorari Denied June 11, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 4370.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Cox, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2190 (Pa., July 29, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Cox v. Pennsylvania, 533 U.S. 904, 121 S. Ct. 2246, 150 L. Ed. 2d 233, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 4370 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Commonwealth v. Cox, 603 Pa. 223, 983 A.2d 666, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 2423 (2009)
Motion denied by Cox v. Horn, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 167382 (E.D. Pa., May 23, 2013)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Cox, 146 A.3d 221, 2016 Pa. LEXIS 2170 (Pa., 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered on April 12, 1995 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Philadelphia County, at No. 9306-2245 and 2249.

Direct Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of Death entered on April 12, 1995 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County at No. 9306-2245 & 2249.
Commonwealth v. Cox, 445 Pa. Super. 624, 664 A.2d 1054, 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1730 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia and directed the Prothonotary to transmit the records to the Governor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of first degree murder, defendant appealed directly to the instant court, raising allegations of trial court error and ineffectiveness of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant raised numerous allegations of trial court error and ineffectiveness of trial counsel. The instant court held that the evidence proved that defendant planned and carried out the killing, clearly satisfying statutory elements of first degree murder, and that the evidence was therefore sufficient to sustain the conviction. Further, the court concluded that the trial court exercised its discretion properly when it dismissed certain potential jurors for cause after they answered positively to certain questions. The failure of defendant's counsel's to cross-examine witnesses concerning bias stemming from an outstanding warrant, criminal charges, probations, or paroles did not so prejudice defendant that the result of the trial would have been different if counsel had pursued this line of questioning. Thus, defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was meritless. The record revealed that defendant's death sentence was not the product of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor and that there was sufficient evidence to support the aggravating circumstances found by the jury.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the death sentence imposed by the trial court, on grounds that the sentence was not the product of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor; and there was sufficient evidence to support the aggravating circumstances found by the jury.

 

19 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Housing Auth. v. Pennsylvania State Civ. Serv. Comm'n


No. 180 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 1997, No. 181 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 621; 730 A.2d 935; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1276


April 29, 1998, Argued  
April 30, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal and Cross-Pettion for Allowance of Appeal Granted, December 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the Order and Published Opinion of the Commonwealth Court, entered March 12, 1997 at 1477 C.D. 1996, reversing the order of the State Civil Service Commission, dated May 17, 1996, at No. 18970, 692 A.2d 1122 (Pa. Commw. 1997).



DISPOSITION: The order of the Commonwealth Court is vacated and this matter is remanded for further proceedings which are consistent with this opinion. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant civil service commission sought review of an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) that reversed appellant's order directing appellee housing authority to offer a job to a veteran who was one of three top candidates. Appellant claimed it had standing to enforce veterans' preference provisions of Military Affairs Act sua sponte, and Act required that position be offered to the veteran.


OVERVIEW: A decision that reversed appellant civil service commission's order requiring appellee housing authority to offer a job to a veteran who was one of the top three candidates was vacated and the case was remanded. Appellant claimed that it had standing to enforce the veterans' preference provisions of the Military Affairs Act, 51 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7101 et seq., sua sponte, and that the Act required that the position be offered to the veteran. The appellate court held that appellant had the authority to enforce the provisions on its own initiative. Appellant's directive under which it acted when challenging appellee's hiring decision was adopted pursuant to appellant's legislative rule-making power. It was deemed valid and binding where it was within the granted power, was issued pursuant to proper procedure, and was reasonable. The court held that the veterans' preference provisions required that the job be offered to the qualified veteran because appellee was not permitted to impose independent job requirements other than successful civil service testing. The provisions were constitutional in the context of appointments to civil service positions.


OUTCOME: A ruling that reversed appellant civil service commission's order directing appellee housing authority to offer a job to a veteran who was a top candidate was vacated and the case was remanded. The veterans' preference provisions of the Military Affairs Act, which required that the job be offered to the veteran, were not unconstitutional in the context of civil service appointments.

 

20 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Haller v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 0049 M.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 289; 728 A.2d 351; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1136


April 28, 1998, Argued  
April 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Commonwealth Court dated May 1, 1997 at No. 241 M.D. 1993, granting petitioners' motion for summary judgment. JUDGES BELOW: DEPT OF REVENUE - / Commonwealth - COLINS, P.J., DOYLE, MCGINLEY, SMITH, PELLEGRINI, KELLEY, NEWMAN, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the commonwealth, the revenue department, and revenue officials, challenged an order from the Order of Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) granting petitioner taxpayers motion for summary judgment in petitioners' constitutional challenge to a sales tax exemption as violative of the Establishment Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I, Pa. Const. art. I, § 3, the Press Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I, and Pa. Const. art. I, § 7.


OVERVIEW: A tax exemption of appellant commonwealth exempted from sales tax the sale at retail or use of religious publications sold by religious groups and Bibles and religious articles. Petitioners successfully challenged the constitutionality of this exemption as violative of the Establishment Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I. This exemption showed a preference for communication of religious messages as had been held unconstitutional by the U.S. Supreme Court in a previous case based upon a lack of breadth of coverage. The exemption did not cover a broad secular purpose, such as the publication of philosophical literature distributed by nonreligious organizations devoted to similar subject matters; nr did the exemption allow for the exemption based upon the type of organization that produced it, as opposed to its content. Therefore, summary judgment for petitioners was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for petitioners was affirmed, where a tax exemption was unconstitutional because it protected the communication of religious messages and lacked a broader secular purpose.

 

21 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Bureau of Prof'l & Occupational Affairs v. State Bd. of Physical Therapy


No. 47 M.D. Appeal Docket 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 268; 728 A.2d 340; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1135


November 17, 1998, Argued  
April 20, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of Commonwealth Court, dated November 25, 1997, denying reconsideration or reargument en banc of the panel opinion and order of October 8, 1997 at docket No. 697 C.D. 1997 701 A.2d 292 (Pa.Cmwlth. 1997). JUDGES BELOW: ST BD PHYICAL THERAPY - / COMMONWEALTH - Kelley, Flaherty, JJ., Silvestri, SJ.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) that prevented them as chiropractors from advertising that they performed physical therapy in an action brought by appellee pursuant to the Physical Therapy Act, 63 Pa. Code § 1304.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the order that prevented appellant chiropractors from advertising that they performed physical therapy. Although chiropractors performed some services that fell within the statutory definition of physical therapy, 63 Pa. Code § 1304, they were not allowed to perform the full range of services that fell within the definition. Moreover, chiropractors had their own distinct range of licensed services. There was no violation of appellants' freedom of expression because appellants' advertising was misleading in light of the statutory definition of the respective licensed services.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court order because it was constitutionally permissible to restrict the content of commercial speech where there was a statutory definition of the services appellants claimed to provide that was used for licensing purposes and which appellants were not licensed to perform.

Commonwealth v. Keaton


154 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 442; 729 A.2d 529; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1015


October 20, 1998, Argued  
April 12, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1162.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Keaton, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1710 (Pa., June 15, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Keaton v. Pennsylvania, 528 U.S. 1163, 120 S. Ct. 1180, 145 L. Ed. 2d 1087, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1162 (Feb. 22, 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at Commonwealth v. Keaton, 968 A.2d 792, 2009 Pa. Super. LEXIS 296 (Pa. Super. Ct., Jan. 30, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by, in part Commonwealth v. Keaton, 615 Pa. 675, 45 A.3d 1050, 2012 Pa. LEXIS 1267 (May 30, 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, Without prejudice Keaton v. Folino, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 92621 (E.D. Pa., June 15, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Judgment of Sentence entered on 9/21/94 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia, Numbers 1925 March Term 1993/Capital Numbers: 1925 March Term 1993. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. Eugene H. Clarke, Jr., S.J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the verdict and sentence of death imposed upon Keaton by the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him to death upon his conviction for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court found that consolidation of the informations against appellant inmate was proper where the similarities between the crimes were sufficient to establish a sufficient logical connection in the form of a common plan, scheme, or design. The appellate court further found that there was no prosecutorial misconduct where appellant failed to show that the unavoidable effect of the remarks during closing argument was to arouse the jurors' emotions or to prejudice them that so they could not fairly weigh the evidence and return a true verdict. Although the appellate court found that the trial court improperly refused to allow defense counsel to ascertain whether the venireperson would automatically impose a sentence of death if the jury returned a first-degree murder conviction, it then held that a new penalty hearing was unwarranted where the error did not deprive appellant of an impartial trial. The appellate court affirmed, finding that, upon an independent review of the death sentence, the sentence was properly based on the evidence presented at trial and was not excessive or disproportionate to the penalties imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the first-degree murder conviction and the death sentence where sufficient evidence existed to show that appellant inmate caused the victim's death during a rape; although trial court erred in refusing to allow the questioning of a venireperson's inability to assess life imprisonment following a first-degree murder conviction, new hearing was unwarranted without a showing that appellant was deprived of an impartial trial.

Commonwealth v. Breakiron


No. 213 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 519; 729 A.2d 1088; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 983


July 20, 1998, Submitted  
April 9, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 22, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1250. Application for Reargument Denied August 16, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2365.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Breakiron, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2365 (Pa., Aug. 16, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Breakiron v. Pennsylvania, 528 U.S. 1169, 120 S. Ct. 1193, 145 L. Ed. 2d 1098, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1250 (2000)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Breakiron, 566 Pa. 323, 781 A.2d 94, 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2075 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division, entered December 22, 1997, at No. 331 of 1987, denying the Petition for Post-Conviction Relief. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. William J. Franks, PJ.
Commonwealth v. Breakiron, 524 Pa. 282, 571 A.2d 1035, 1990 Pa. LEXIS 65 (1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed a woman, then took her purse and bags. Defendant's sole defense at trial was diminished capacity. He was convicted of first-degree murder and robbery. The jury sentenced defendant to death, finding two aggravating circumstances: that the victim was tortured and that the murder was committed in the course of a robbery. Defendant filed a petition for post conviction relief, alleging claims of ineffective assistance of counsel and trial court error. The court denied relieve, holding defendants' claims were either waived, previously litigated or were without merit. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief. The court disagreed with defendant that the Attorney General's office had any actual conflict in the matter. The court also found defendant's claim attacking the effectiveness of his trial counsel was without merit. Defendant did not show that a claimed error in a jury instruction prejudiced him. Trial counsel also articulated a reasonable trial strategy. The court did not find that any of counsel's mishandling of defendant's mental health issues were prejudicial to defendant at either the guilt or sentencing phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, finding there was no merit to defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of his counsel.

Commonwealth v. O'Shea


No. 171 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


556 Pa. 6; 726 A.2d 376; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 573


October 5, 1998, Submitted  
March 4, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied April 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1069.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas entered May 1, 1997 at Nos. CC8512675A and CC8512903A. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. Robert P. Horgos.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), denying his petition for postconviction relief related to his convictions for robbery and first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of robbery and first degree murder, and he was sentenced to death. Appellant's petition for postconviction relief was denied. On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court's jury instructions and verdict sheet unconstitutionally indicated that the jury had to find a mitigating circumstance unanimously before it could give effect to such a circumstance in its sentencing decision. Appellant further argued that his trial and appellate counsel were ineffective in failing to pursue the issue of the trial judge's recusal on grounds of federal law. The court ruled that appellant was ineligible for postconviction relief based on his claim that the jury instructions and verdict sheet were unconstitutional pursuant to Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9543 (a)(3) because the court previously addressed the issue on direct appeal. The court affirmed the denial of appellant's petition for postconviction relief and affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence concluding that his argument for recusal relied entirely on federal statutes and caselaw, which had no application in a case prosecuted in state court.


OUTCOME: Order denying appellant's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed where the court addressed appellant's argument that the jury instructions and verdict sheet were unconstitutional on direct appeal, and appellant's argument that his counsel were ineffective inappropriately relied entirely on federal law.

Commonwealth v. Blystone


No. 136 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 565; 725 A.2d 1197; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 487


February 3, 1997, Submitted  
February 26, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Blystone, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1522 (Pa., May 28, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, dated January 4, 1996, denying appellant's petition for post-conviction relief from the judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County at Nos. 2, 2 1/4, 2 2/4, 2 3/4 of 1984 term. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Conrad B. Capuzzi.
Commonwealth v. Blystone, 519 Pa. 450, 549 A.2d 81, 1988 Pa. LEXIS 243 (1988)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Common Pleas Court, Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's petition for post-conviction relief on convictions of murder, robbery, and conspiracy for which the death penalty was imposed, under the Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9543 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The lower court correctly denied defendant's petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., from his convictions of murder, robbery, and conspiracy and the resultant death sentence. The court agreed that the record did not support appellant's position that jurors may have been excused for cause after having expressed only generalized opposition to the death penalty. Any request for transcription of the stenographic notes of voir dire would be frivolous where no specific claim of error was made. Life-qualification of jurors was barred by appellant's exhaustion of direct appeals before the rule was announced. Appellant failed to demonstrate the lower court's requirements for the exercise of peremptory challenges undermined reliable adjudication. Claims previously litigated on direct appeal warranted no relief and appellant failed to show he was prejudiced by ineffective assistance of counsel. Appellant's failure to testify as to mitigation was his choice, penalty-phase jury instructions correctly tracked the statute, anti-sympathy instructions were not barred, and, where individual claims failed, collective claims did also.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed because life-qualification of jurors was barred by the exhaustion of direct appeals before the rule was announced, claims litigated on direct appeal warranted no relief, the lower court's preemptory challenge procedures did not undermine reliable adjudication, and appellant failed to show he was prejudiced by ineffective assistance of counsel.

Commonwealth v. Cross


No. 179 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 603; 726 A.2d 333; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 526


March 9, 1998, Submitted  
February 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied April 21, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1253.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Cross, 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1253 (Pa., Apr. 21, 1999)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Cross v. Price, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18510 (W.D. Pa., Aug. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct appeal from the Order entered on March 6, 1997, by the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County, Pennsylvania at Nos. 565 A, B. & C of 1981.
Cross v. Pennsylvania, 513 U.S. 833, 130 L. Ed. 2d 56, 115 S. Ct. 109, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 5760 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County (Pennsylvania), denying appellant's petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of murder, was sentenced to death. Direct review of the sentence ended in 1985. Appellant filed a petition under the Post-Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., in 1991, which was denied. Appellant filed a second PCRA petition in 1997, attaching a testifying psychiatrist's affidavit stating that his opinion of appellant's mental state at the time of the murders would have differed had he examined appellant for another hour. The trial court denied the petition; on appeal, the court affirmed. The petition was not timely; it was not filed within a year of the final judgment, nor could appellant avail himself of the provision allowing for the filing of a first petition within one year of the PCRA's effective date, January 16, 1996, because the instant petition was his second. Appellant was not entitled to an exception to the one-year filing requirement; the claim did not hinge upon changed facts, and due diligence would have revealed the facts underlying the psychiatrist's opinion. The jury instruction regarding mitigating circumstances was proper as it copied the language of the death penalty statute, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(c)(iv).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief; appellant's second petition was not timely as it was not filed within a year of final judgment, appellant could not file a second petition within a year of the statute's effective date, and no exceptions applied; the jury instruction concerning the determination of mitigating circumstances was constitutional.

 

27 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Kimball


38 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 299; 724 A.2d 326; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 134


October 23, 1997, Submitted  
January 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied March 10, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 635.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court entered September 19, 1996 at No. 952PHL95 Reversing/Vacating and Remanding the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northumberland County, entered February 15, 1995 at Nos. 30 C 1989 and 31 C 1989. 683 A.2d 666 (Pa. Super. 1996). JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Honorable Barry F. Feudale, P.J. / SUPERIOR - MCEWEN, P.J., DEL SOLE, BECK, TAMILIA, KELLEY, POPOVICH, JOHNSON, HUDOCK AND SCHILLER, JJ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) which reversed, vacated, and remanded the order of the trial court finding that defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective.


OVERVIEW: The state appealed from the superior court's judgment that defendant's trial counsel had been ineffective. The supreme court declined to impose a more stringent prejudice requirement than that applicable to direct appeals, but, nevertheless, found that defendant failed to demonstrate that his trial counsel was ineffective at trial. The court found that although defense counsel was aware of the agreement the state had with defendant's cellmate, defense counsel did not cross-examine defendant's cellmate concerning the deal he made with the state. However, defense counsel did elicit from the witness other information used to impeach his credibility. The court additionally found that eliciting purportedly damaging testimony from defendant's adoptive father did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel. The admission of the testimony had not so prejudiced defendant as to render the verdict unreliable. Defendant failed to establish his counsel's ineffectiveness pursuant to the standard set forth in 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9543(a)(2)(ii), therefore, the court reversed the order of the superior court and reinstated the order of the post conviction relief court, and denied relief.


OUTCOME: Judgment that defendant was denied effective assistance of counsel was reversed and the order of the trial court, denying defendant relief, was reinstated. Defendant failed to establish his counsel's ineffectiveness pursuant to the standard set forth in the applicable statute, although the statutory language did not create a higher burden on defendant in his post conviction proceeding.

 

28 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Parsowith v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 172 M.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 200; 723 A.2d 659; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 112


November 16, 1998, Argued  
January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of Commonwealth Court entered 11/7/97 at 347 M.D. 1997 sustaining preliminary objections and dismissing the Petition for Review from order of Board of Finance and Revenue. JUDGES BELOW: BD FINANCE/REVENUE - / Commonwealth - Flaherty, Leadbetter, JJ., LORD, SJ.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Commonwealth Court is reversed, and the case is remanded for entry of judgment on the merits in favor of the Commonwealth, Department of Revenue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, executrix of her husband's estate, sought review of an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's claim that the Inheritance and Estate Tax Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 9101-9196, was unconstitutional in allowing appellee revenue agency to apply a higher tax rate to wrongful death proceeds she received after her husband's 1993 death than the rate applied after the 1995 amendments became effective.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, executrix of her husband's estate, argued trial court error in dismissing her claim challenging the constitutionality of the Inheritance and Estate Tax Act (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, §§ 9101-9196, under the uniformity clause of Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1, simply because appellant did not exhaust her administrative remedies in contesting a lower tax rate applied to wrongful death proceeds attributable to decedents dying after -- but not before -- the 1995 amendments, a rate unavailable to appellant due to her husband's 1993 death. The court agreed, ruling that an administrative appeal would be futile in view of appellant's direct attack on the statutory scheme of taxation, as opposed to an attack on an administrative interpretation. Courts need not adhere to the prescribed administrative process when the claim could only be resolved in a judicial forum. In addressing the uniformity issue, the court upheld the Act as being rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. Use of a decedent's date of death was a legitimate benchmark for inheritance taxation, the court concluded, as it promoted timely, orderly, and efficient revenue collection and estate administration.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing claim of appellant, executrix of husband's estate, that inheritance law was unconstitutional in allowing appellee agency to apply a higher tax rate to wrongful death proceeds she received after husband's 1993 death than rate applied after law's 1995 amendments reversed, as appellant allowed to bypass administrative process lacking authority to pass on constitutional claims, and as act was related to a legitimate state purpose.

Commonwealth v. Hendrickson


Nos. 73-75 W.D. Appeal Dkt. 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 277; 724 A.2d 315; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 123


March 11, 1998, Argued  
January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court Nos. 407-409PGH95 entered October 15, 1996 affirming the Judgments of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division at Nos. CC 92-04507, CC 92-04515, CC 92-03772, CC 92-05037, entered September 27, 1994. 453 Pa. Super. 533, 684 A.2d 171.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) that upheld appellant's conviction of harassment by communication or address in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5504.


OVERVIEW: Appellant anonymously sent messages to about 40 people at their offices by facsimile. The faxed messages contained racial and ethnic statements and derogatory comments about the medical and legal professions. The recipients testified that the faxes disrupted their offices and invoked emotions of anger and fear. Appellant was charged and convicted of multiple counts of harassment by communication or address under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5504(a)(1). Appellant argued that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the plain language of the statute was not directed at the content of speech, but simply sought to regulate conduct intended to harass another, and that the government had a legitimate interest in preventing the harassment of individuals. The statute was sufficiently specific in stating what was prohibited and thus was not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of harassment by communication or address. The court held that the statute was sufficiently specific in stating what was prohibited and was therefore not impermissibly vague, and that the statute was not directed at the content of speech but simply sought to regulate conduct.

 

30 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Arroyo


190 M.D. App. Dkt. 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 125; 723 A.2d 162; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 125


October 23, 1997, Argued  
January 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court filed on June 17, 1996, in the matter docketed at No. 2029 Philadelphia 1995 affirming the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, entered on May 10, 1995 in the matter docketed at Criminal No. 3154-19941994. JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Hon. Paul K. Allison / Superior - CAVANAUGH, EAKIN, OLSZEWSKI, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court, Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first-degree murder and denied defendant's motion to suppress his confession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to the police station to be interviewed about the circumstances that surrounded the death of his son. Defendant waived his Miranda rights and was interrogated. During the interrogation, an attorney called and requested to speak with defendant to determine if defendant wanted counsel. The police did not inform defendant that an attorney called him. Defendant confessed that he caused the death of his son. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the conviction, and he was convicted of first-degree murder. The intermediate appellate court affirmed. The court affirmed because the right to counsel under Pa. Const. art. I, § 9, was identical to the right to counsel provided by U.S. Const. amend. V and that right did not attach until formal initiation of adversarial judicial proceedings occurred. Because defendant consented to the interview and waived his Miranda rights, his right to counsel was not violated. The court found the expert witness had a reasonable pretension to knowledge in the specialized areas on which he testified, thus, there was no abuse of discretion when the trial court admitted the expert testimony.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the intermediate appellate court that found defendant's conviction was proper was affirmed because defendant's right to counsel did not attach until there was a formal initiation of adversarial judicial proceedings, and defendant waived his Miranda right to counsel before he confessed to the crime.

 

31 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Coyne


No. 94 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997, No. 96 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997, No. 97 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


555 Pa. 21; 722 A.2d 1022; 1999 Pa. LEXIS 116


September 15, 1998, Argued  
January 19, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Pennsylvania, Civil Division, at No. GD 97-4011 dated October 28, 1997 and entered October 29, 1997.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the court of common pleas is vacated and the cases are remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, landlords and landlord associations, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) holding that the requirements for supersedeas under Pa. R. Civ. P. Dist. J. 1008B violated the appellee low-income tenants' right to a jury trial under Pa. Const. art. I, § 6, in a consolidated appeal of nine landlord-tenant cases raising the identical issue.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, landlords, and landlord associations, challenged an order of the trial court striking down as unconstitutional certain provisions of Pa. R. Civ. P. Dist. J. 1008B, as applied to low-income persons in a landlord-tenant action. Rule 1008B stated that a tenant's appeal from a judgment of a district justice granting possession of the property to the landlord operated as a supersedeas only if the tenant deposited a sum of money with the court. The trial court held that this provision effectively denied a jury trial to those who could not pay arrears and would likely be evicted, thereby violating Pa. Const. art. I, § 6. In reversing, the court held that in balancing the rights of tenants and landlords, the landlord's right to possess and control his property had greater constitutional weight than the tenant's right to a jury trial, and that Rule 1008B did not, therefore, unconstitutionally burden tenants' right to a jury trial or violate their due process rights. The court further held that because the protection of the landlord's property was a rational basis for the requirements of the rule, the provisions did not violate the equal protection rights of low-income tenants.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment finding that certain provisions of the rules of court regarding appeals from landlord-tenant cases were unconstitutional and remanded the nine consolidated cases for proceedings, holding that the rights of the landlord to his property outweighed the rights of a tenant to a jury trial, and that therefore the rules of court did not violate a tenant's rights to jury trial, due process or equal protection.

Small v. Horn


79 M.D. Appeal Dkt. 1998


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


554 Pa. 600; 722 A.2d 664; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2720


September 8, 1998, Submitted  
December 23, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated May 7, 1998, at 135 M.D. 1998 dismissing Petition for Review and dismissing Petition to Intervene as moot.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates sought review of an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which sustained appellee state's preliminary objections in appellants' action that sought to invalidate appellee's revocation of their permission to wear civilian clothing while housed in the general population. The trial court also dismissed intervenor's petition to intervene as moot.


OVERVIEW: Appellee department entered into a consent decree whereby it was required to permit prisoners to wear civilian clothing when housed in the general population. Subsequently, the decree terminated and appellee amended certain bulletins, which provided prisoners with a restricted list of suitable garments. Appellant inmates sued asserting that the bulletins were regulations and as such should have been promulgated pursuant to the Commonwealth Documents Law, 45 Pa. Const. Stat. §§ 1102-1602, and the regulatory oversight provisions. The trial court sustained appellee's preliminary objections and dismissed the complaint. On review, the court found that the bulletins were business-type decisions, which were not amenable to the normal public participation process, and not subject to the Documents Law. Further, the court found that appellants had not stated a cause of action under the Due Process Clause because the issuance of the bulletins was not an adjudication. Finally, the court concluded that the bulletins did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. Accordingly, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order, which sustained appellee department's preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer, dismissed appellant's petition for review, and dismissed as moot intervenor's petition to intervene was affirmed because the court, in accepting all material facts set forth in the complaint and all inferences fairly deducible from those facts as true, concluded that appellants were not entitled to relief.

Commonwealth v. Lester

Post-conviction relief dismissed at, Sub nomine at Commonwealth v. Ali, 2012 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 407 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of Death entered April 12, 1995 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, at 90-11-0300-307. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Ricardo C. Jackson.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's death sentence, finding that the evidence amply demonstrated that he committed the murder with the requisite intent and deliberation to sustain his first degree murder conviction. Appellant had beaten, scalded, and drowned his victim. The court also rejected appellant's allegations of trial court error, as well as his challenge to the constitutionality of the death penalty statute.
