Commonwealth v. Peterkin


No. 0165 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


554 Pa. 547; 722 A.2d 638; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2697


August 11, 1998, Submitted  
December 21, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order dated January 23, 1997, of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia, at Nos. 784-793, February Term 1982, Capital Nos. 784-8202. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. Alfred F. Sabo.



DISPOSITION: Because appellant's PCRA petition was filed out of time, and we have found the PCRA time limitation and its exceptions constitutional, and because none of the appellant's allegations falls within the statutory exceptions to the one-year time limitation of the PCRA, we conclude that the petition was properly dismissed, albeit for a reason different from that given by the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), in which the trial court denied appellant's second petition for postconviction relief on the grounds that the petition was premature due to ongoing habeas corpus litigation in federal court.


OVERVIEW: While a federal habeas corpus petition was pending, appellant filed a second petition for postconviction relief from his first degree murder convictions that was also captioned as a request for habeas relief. The trial court dismissed the petition as premature due to the ongoing federal litigation. The court affirmed on other grounds, holding that appellant's petition was untimely and the allegations did not fall within the statutory exceptions to the time limitation under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA). In rejecting appellant's assertion that habeas corpus relief was constitutionally guaranteed and could not be suspended by the PCRA, the court explained the writ continued to exist only where there was no remedy under the PCRA. Appellant's claims of constitutional violations and of law that undermined the truth-determining process were cognizable under the PCRA. Pennsylvania' s statutory writ of habeas corpus, therefore, was not available. Further, the PCRA's time limitation did not unconstitutionally limit appellant's right to habeas corpus relief because it struck a reasonable balance between the need for finality and the need to demonstrate error in the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying appellant's second petition for postconviction relief on other grounds, holding that the petition was properly dismissed because appellant's petition was filed out of time, the allegations did not fall within the statutory exceptions to the one year time limit, and the PCRA time limitation and its exceptions were constitutional.

Commonwealth v. Rompilla


152 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


554 Pa. 378; 721 A.2d 786; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2624

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction, entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Lehigh County (Pennsylvania), for capital murder and of his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Appellant stabbed his victim repeatedly and set him on fire. The court rejected appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim because appellant's counsel chose not to present evidence of appellant's alleged mental infirmity at the punishment phase since three of appellant's own experts reported that appellant was a sociopath. The court held that the prosecutor's comment that the jury should show appellant the same mercy appellant showed his victim was permissible during the penalty phase. The court found that other comments by the prosecutor did not have the unavoidable effect of arousing the jury's emotions or prejudice the jury so they could not fairly weigh the evidence. The court found that the word "torture" in the trial court's instruction on aggravating circumstances was not vague because the meaning of the word was common knowledge. The court determined that it was proper for the trial court to have allowed the prosecutor to read to the jury, during the penalty phase, the testimony of a rape victim of appellant. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of murder in the first degree and sentence of death because appellant received effective assistance of counsel, and the prosecutor did not make improper comments to the jury.

Post-conviction proceeding at, Stay granted by Commonwealth v. King, 2000 Pa. LEXIS 563 (Pa., Mar. 13, 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Stay granted by Commonwealth v. Martin, 2000 Pa. LEXIS 562 (Pa., Mar. 13, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the judgment of sentence entered on November 30, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County, Criminal 93-10898. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. Robert J. Eby.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the verdicts and sentences of death imposed upon Bradley Martin and Carolyn King by the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Co-defendants consolidated direct appeals from death sentences imposed by judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Lebanon County (Pennsylvania), after the jury found that all of the aggravating circumstances presented with respect to each defendant had been established, found no mitigating circumstances for either defendant, and found each defendant guilty of first-degree murder and related offenses.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of co-defendants' convictions and death sentences for first degree murder and related offenses, multiple challenges were overruled when the court affirmed the trial court judgment. The court found the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions of first-degree murder of a victim who had been bound, and suffocated during an attempted robbery. Though both defendants attempted to exculpate themselves by directing blame to other defendant, such finger pointing alone was insufficient to warrant separate trials. The trial court properly admitted evidence of an escape from prison that was part of the chain or sequence of events that resulted in the murder. Also, the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it admitted photographic evidence that depicted the manner in which the victim was bound, because it was essential to the intent element of first-degree murder. Finally, the proven aggravated circumstances found by the jury supported the sentence notwithstanding the court's error in the aggravated circumstance of torture under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(d)(8) that could not be considered because it was presented through expert testimony, improperly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed verdicts and death sentences imposed upon co-defendants for first-degree murder and related offenses as supported by the evidence. The trial court's error during the penalty phase when it allowed expert testimony on torture, although circumstances of the killing provided sufficient evidence for the jury to have inferred an intent to torture the victim, was not fatal. Other proven aggravated circumstances supported the sentence.

The inmate argued that the appropriate remedy was a remand to the PCRA court for appointment of substitute counsel to brief the issues waived in that court. The reviewing court found that such relief was inappropriate since the inmate was not denied the right to appeal. None of the inmate's claims of ineffective assistance were successful.

Pap's A.M. v. City of Erie


Nos. 16 Western District Appeal Docket 1997, 17 Western District Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


553 Pa. 348; 719 A.2d 273; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2307


September 16, 1997, Argued  
October 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Granted May 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3201.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, dated march 27, 1996 at Nos. 445 and 446 C.D. 1995, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, dated January 18, 1995 at No. 60059 of 1994. 674 A.2d 338 (Pa. Commw. Ct. 1996). JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Honorable Shad Connelly, A.J. / COMMONWEALTH - DOYLE, Smith, Mirarchi, S.J., JJ.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nightclub operator challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, which reversed a lower court's injunction against the enforcement of Erie, Pa., Ordinance 75-1994 (1994), striking down in its entirety the ordinance that was enacted by appellees, mayor and city council members. Appellant filed a petition for allowance of appeal with the highest state court.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, mayor and city council members, enacted Erie, Pa., Ordinance 75-1994 (1994), which provided that it was a summary offense to appear in a state of nudity. In order to avoid being in a state of nudity, a female person over the age of 10 years of age had to wear, at a minimum, pasties and a G-string. Appellant nightclub operator, which had an establishment that featured nude female erotic dancing, filed a complaint against appellees, requesting a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutional and seeking injunctive relief and attorney fees. The trial court determined that ordinance was unconstitutionally overbroad on its face. A permanent injunction was granted, and the ordinance was struck down. However, appellant's request for attorney fees was denied. On cross-appeals, the trial court's order striking the ordinance and awarding appellant injunctive relief was reversed. Appellant filed a petition for allowance of appeal with the highest state court. The appellate court's order was reversed, because the ordinance placed an unconstitutional burden on appellant's freedom of expression based on appellees' failure to pass strict scrutiny test.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's order was reversed because appellees' nudity ordinance was unconstitutional unless the public nudity bar was severed since the negative secondary effects associated with appellant's nude dance club were inextricably linked to erotic message of the dance, thus, appellees' content-neutral reason for ordinance was insufficient to save full ordinance because it was linked with a content-based motivation for restriction.

Commonwealth v. Williams

Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Williams, 594 Pa. 366, 936 A.2d 12, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2440 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgments of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section, Imposed on Nos. 1770, 1772, 1776, 1778, 1788, 1790, 1796, 1825, 1827, 1833, 1846, April Term, 1992. JUDGE BELOW: Honorable Paul Ribner.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Criminal Section (Pennsylvania), convicting defendant of murder and related offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by the trial court, following a jury trial, of murder and related offenses. Defendant sought review of the trial court judgment, asserting numerous errors, including that the verdicts were against the weight of the evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the evidence of record was more than sufficient to establish that defendant was guilty of three counts of first-degree murder. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in dismissing two jurors due to unexplained tardiness and due to a scheduling conflict. The court additionally did not err when it refused to sever defendant's trial from that of his alleged co-conspirators because separate trials of co-defendants should be granted only where the defenses of each are antagonistic to the point where such individual differences are irreconcilable and a joint trial would result in prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of murder and related offenses, holding that the record evidence was sufficient to support the judgment against him.

 

41 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Stilp v. Hafer


No. 169 M.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


553 Pa. 128; 718 A.2d 290; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2119


March 13, 1998, Submitted  
October 1, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated November 7, 1997, at No. 336 M.D. 1996. JUDGES BELOW: COMMONWEALTH - KELLEY, Flaherty, JJ & Silvestri, SJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens challenged the summary judgment entered by the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania) in favor of appellee commonwealth, in appellants' action for injunctive and declaratory relief with respect to alleged procedural irregularities in the enactment of the Low-Level Radioactive Waste Disposal Act, 35 P.S. § 7130.101-7130.905 (1993). Appellant argued that laches could not be used to defeat a constitutional challenge to a statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant citizens sought equitable relief against appellee Commonwealth and alleged that the procedures of Pa. Const. art. III were violated when the Low-Level Radioactive Waste Disposal Act, 35 P.S. § 7130.101-7130.905 (1993), was enacted. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellee based upon the doctrine of laches. On review, appellants claimed that laches could not be used to defeat a constitutional challenge to a statute. Appellants also argued that if laches did apply, appellee did not establish the requisite elements of the doctrine. The court disagreed, and held that a challenge to a statute based upon procedural deficiencies in its enactment could be barred by laches. The court reasoned that the processes that were available to the public when a new law was enacted prevented statutes that were constitutionally sound and relied upon by citizens from being continually revisited by courts. The court also concluded that appellants did not act diligently in pursuing their claim and that appellee established prejudice as a result of the eight-year delay between the statute's enactment and appellants' suit. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment entered for appellee commonwealth on grounds that laches barred appellant citizens' complaint was affirmed, because the doctrine of laches could bar a challenge to a statute based upon procedural deficiencies in its enactment. Appellants did not pursue their claim diligently, and appellee was prejudiced by the eight-year delay between appellants' complaint and the enactment of the statute.

Commonwealth v. Crews


No. 196 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


552 Pa. 659; 717 A.2d 487; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 1769

August 20, 1998, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered on July 22, 1997 in the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, C.A. No. 318 of 1990. Direct Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, Pennsylvania, denying P.C.R.A. Relief Entered July 22, 1997 at No. 318 of 1990 (Quigley, J.) JUDGE BEWLO: Hon. Keith B. Quigley, PJ.
Commonwealth v. Crews, 1994 Pa. LEXIS 173 (Pa., May 31, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a direct appeal from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County (Pennsylvania) that denied him relief under the the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546, in a capital case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Defendant filed a petition under the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9546, claiming that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel because counsel failed to argue that the death penalty constituted cruel and unusual punishment, that under Pennsylvania's death penalty statute, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711, the sentencing jury was given an inappropriate degree of discretion, and that the death penalty was predominantly imposed upon the poor. Moreover, the court held that all of defendant's other claims were properly dismissed because they were litigated previously.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court denying defendant relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act because it concluded that the claims raised by defendant were either previously litigated or were without merit.

The court held that appellee, Department of Environmental Protection, could require an owner or occupier of land to correct a condition which existed regardless of whether they had prior knowledge of such condition.

Ligonier Tavern v. Workmen's Comp. Appeal Bd. (walker)

552 Pa. 237; 714 A.2d 1008; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 1421


September 16, 1997, Argued  
July 20, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court dated July 26, 1996, at No. 2046 C.D. 1995, affirming the Order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board dated July 18, 1995, at No. A94-0440. 681 A.2d 222 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1996). JUDGE(S) BELOW: WORKMEN'S COMPENSATION APPEAL BOARD - / COMMONWEALTH - McGinley, FLAHERTY, Rodgers, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order from appellee Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board for appellee claimant, in a case regarding additional worker's compensation for a minor.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that ordered a minor to be compensated an additional fifty percent of her weekly compensation because it found that appellant employer had violated the Child Labor Law, 43 P.S. § 49. The court found that appellant had failed to obtain a work permit for appellee claimant, a minor, and § 49 required appellant to obtain an employment certificate. The court held that the 77 P.S. § 320 did not violate Pa. Const. art. The court held that § 320 also did not violate the equal protection clause, Pa. Const. art. III, § 32, because application of the statute to all minors constituted a reasonable and logical means of achieving the purpose of the Child Labor Law. The court held that § 320 applied to all minors under the age of eighteen and did not constitute special legislation since the classification did not interfere with a fundamental right or disadvantageously affect a suspect class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court order, which held that appellee claimant was entitled to an additional fifty percent compensation because the Child Labor Law allowed for the compensation for violation of the statute and the statute was not unconstitutional.

Commonwealth v. Lesko


No. 144 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


553 Pa. 233; 719 A.2d 217; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 1022


September 15, 1997, Submitted  
May 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Commonwealth v. Lesko, 609 Pa. 128, 15 A.3d 345, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 392 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the sentence of death imposed by the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, at No. 681 C 1980, dated February 17, 1995. JUDGE BELOW: CCP - Honorable Gary P. Caruso.
Lesko v. Lehman, 1992 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1123 (W.D. Pa., Jan. 23, 1992)



DISPOSITION: The death sentence imposed by the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which sentenced defendant to death pursuant to a murder conviction, after his original sentence was reversed and his case remanded for a resentencing proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a habeas corpus proceeding, defendant's death sentence arising from a murder conviction was reversed and remanded for resentencing. Upon a resentencing proceeding, defendant was again sentenced to death and appealed the judgment of the trial court. Addressing defendant's multiple contentions of error, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(h)(4), a new sentencing hearing had to be conducted where a sentence of death was vacated, except where it was vacated for lack of evidence of aggravating factors, and that a remand for imposition of a life sentence did not follow the reversal. The court held that the record supported the aggravating circumstances found by the jury and that there was no basis to find that the death sentence was the product of passion, prejudice or any other arbitrary factor. Finding evidence relating to character as being at the core of the sentencing decision, the court held that the commonwealth's comments at the sentencing hearing did not invite retaliatory sentencing, but invited the jury to consider all the relevant facts including defendant's unmerciful character.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which sentenced defendant to death pursuant to a murder conviction, after his original sentence was reversed and his case remanded for a resentencing proceeding. The court held that the record supported the aggravating factors found by the jury in imposing the death penalty and that defendant's sentence was proportionate to sentences imposed in similar cases.

Annenberg v. Commonwealth


No. 003 & 004 Miscellaneous Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


562 Pa. 570; 757 A.2d 333; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 652


May 15, 1997, Submitted  
April 7, 1998, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers sought the plenary jurisdiction of the court under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 726 in its action against respondents, state, state attorney general, and a county board of commissioners, to determine whether Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 4821, that imposed a personal property tax on stock issued by foreign corporations, violated the Commerce Clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayers owned a large amount of stock issued by foreign corporations, and sued respondents, a state, its attorney general, and a county board of commissioners, in the appellate court under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 42, § 761 for an order declaring that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 72, § 4821 was unconstitutional. The appellate court declined jurisdiction, and petitioners sought the court's plenary jurisdiction over the matter under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 726. The court held that because § 4281 imposed a personal property tax on the stock of foreign corporations that did no business in or have a taxable nexus with Pennsylvania, and because foreign corporations included all corporations that were not incorporated in Pennsylvania, § 4821 facially discriminated against interstate commerce. However, if the § 4821 tax was substantially similar to, and the amount of the tax did not exceed, an identifiable intrastate tax, then § 4821 was a compensatory tax and valid under the Commerce Clause of U.S. Const. art. 8, cl. 3. Therefore, the court transferred the case to the county trial court to determine if the tax in § 4821 was compensatory.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to the trial court to determine if the property tax imposed on stock issued by foreign corporations was similar to an identifiable intrastate tax and was thus a compensatory tax. The court held that the tax on foreign stock facially discriminated against interstate commerce, but if the tax was determined to be compensatory, then it did not violate the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution.

SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


551 Pa. 295; 710 A.2d 49; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 640

April 6, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered April 24, 1996 at 1016 C.D. 1995 reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County dated April 5, 1995 at No. 5192 Equity. 675 A.2d. 758 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1996). JUDGES BELOW: CCP - Hon. Richard A. Lewis, J. / COMMONWEALTH - COLINS, P.J., DOYLE, MCGINLEY, SMITH, PELLEGRINI, FRIEDMAN, KELLEY, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Order of the Commonwealth Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and individual taxpayers challenged an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), that upheld a tax imposed by appellee school district on rental consideration paid to lease tax exempt realty after reversing the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County.


OVERVIEW: Appellee school district imposed a tax on rental consideration paid for the privilege of leasing tax exempt realty from appellant city, and appellants city and individual taxpayers challenged the validity of the tax in the trial court, where it was found to be invalid. However, the commonwealth court reversed the trial court and upheld the tax. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the commonwealth court, holding that the tax was invalid because it distinguished between lessees of public and nonpublic property without a reasonable and just basis for the difference in treatment. Therefore, the tax violated the Uniformity Clause, Pa. Const. art. VII, § 1. The court determined that appellee had the power to tax the privilege of leasing public property to raise revenue for general purposes, even in the absence of a tax on the identical privilege on private or nonexempt property under 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5020-204. However, the record did not demonstrate that the unequal tax treatment of lessees of public and nonpublic property was based upon a legitimate distinction in the classification; thus, the tax was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the commonwealth court upholding a tax imposed by appellee school district on rental consideration paid to lease tax exempt realty and found the tax to be invalid because it distinguished between lessees of public and nonpublic property without a reasonable and just basis for the difference in treatment.

Commonwealth v. Bardo


No. 89 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


551 Pa. 140; 709 A.2d 871; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 206


October 25, 1995, Argued  
February 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied May 13, 1998. Application for Reargument Denied May 12, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Pa. LEXIS 959.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Bardo, 1998 Pa. LEXIS 959 (Pa., May 12, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Bardo v. Pennsylvania, 525 U.S. 936, 119 S. Ct. 350, 142 L. Ed. 2d 289, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6573 (1998)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part Commonwealth v. Bardo, 2014 Pa. LEXIS 3364 (Pa., Dec. 16, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County, at No. 2778 of 1992, entered December 15, 1994. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Patrick J. Toole, Jr.



DISPOSITION: The sentence of death is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of first-degree murder under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502 and aggravated indecent assault under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3125. Defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: After being convicted of first-degree murder under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502 and aggravated indecent assault under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3125, defendant was sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant argued that his confession was not admissible as to both crimes, that he was entitled to a mercy instruction, and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain a conviction of first-degree murder. The court affirmed and held that the circumstantial evidence introduced by the commonwealth supported the conclusion that the child was murdered. Further, under the closely related crime exception to the corpus delicti rule, defendant's confession was admissible as to both crimes because the relationship between the two crimes was close and the policy underlying the corpus delicti rule was not violated. The court also found that defendant was not entitled to a mercy instruction and that the jury was properly instructed that if the aggravating circumstances did not outweigh the mitigating circumstances, it was required to impose a life sentence. Finally, the evidence, coupled with defendant's confession, was sufficient to establish that the killing was intentional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the imposition of the death penalty. Under the closely related crime exception defendant's confession was admissible as to both crimes and the commonwealth was not required to introduce evidence of the sexual assault before introducing his confession. Defendant was not entitled to a mercy instruction and the evidence was sufficient to support the first-degree murder conviction.

Stat. § 903(a) for involving his daughter and her friend in the payment. Cons. Stat. § 302.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision holding that appellant could be convicted under the general bribery statute because appellee commonwealth had to prove the element of violation of a known legal duty in addition to the required elements under the State Ethics Act and the State Adverse Interest Act.

Sullivan v. DOT


No. 0023 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


550 Pa. 639; 708 A.2d 481; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 165


September 18, 1997, Argued  
February 26, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court entered July 29, 1996 at No. 2786 C.D. 95 affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, entered September 20, 1995 at No. S.A. 2008 of 1995, 682 A.2d 5 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1996). JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Honorable Robert A. Doyle, S.J. / COMMONWEALTH - COLINS, P.J., McGinley, Smith, Pellegrini, Friedman, Flaherty, Leadbetter, JJ.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the Commonwealth Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, Bureau of Driver Licensing sought review of a judgment of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an order of the trial court sustaining appellee driver's statutory appeal of a one-year license suspension imposed pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1532(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver, a resident and licensed driver of Pennsylvania, was convicted of driving under the influence (DUI) in Nebraska, which was a party to the Driver License Compact of 1961 (Compact). Nebraska reported appellee's conviction to appellant Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, Bureau of Driver Licensing, which informed appellee that his license was being suspended for one year pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1532(b)(3), based on his DUI conviction. The notice made no reference to the Compact. The trial court sustained appellee's challenge, and the appellate court concluded that the state had not enacted the Compact into law as required by Driver License Compact of 1961, art. VIII, § 1; thus, appellant lacked the authority to suspend appellee's license based on his conviction in Nebraska. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court because appellant suspended appellee's license more than a year before the legislature enacted the Compact into law pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1581. Consequently, appellant lacked the authority to suspend appellee's license based on his out-of-state DUI conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed because at the time of appellee driver's license suspension, appellant Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation, Bureau of Driver Licensing did not have the authority to suspend a driver's license based on an out-of-state conviction pursuant to the applicable statute. At the relevant time, the state had not enacted the statute into law.

Commonwealth v. Jermyn


No. 134 Capital Appeal Docket, No. 156 E.D. Misc. Dkt. 1995

January 2, 1997, Submitted  
February 25, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, entered on January 4, 1996 at 15 Criminal Term 1985, denying post-conviction relief. Appeal from the order entered on September 7, 1995, finding appellant competent to be executed.

Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, Pennsylvania, Entered January 4, 1996 at 15 Criminal Term 1985, Denying Post Conviction Relief. Appeal from the Finding Entered on September 7, 1995, Regarding Appellant's Competency to be Executed. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Edgar Bayley.



DISPOSITION: The orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania) that denied his petition for relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA) and found that he was competent to be executed after he was found guilty of first degree murder and given a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of first degree murder for killing his mother and sentenced to death. He was also convicted of arson and aggravated assault. The court affirmed the convictions and judgments of sentence on direct appeal and thereafter affirmed the trial court's dismissal of appellant's first post conviction relief act (PCRA) petition. Appellant then filed a motion to stay execution. The motion was denied as well as the appeal on the denial with the court concluding that the evidence in the record supported the finding that appellant was competent to be executed. A governor's warrant for the execution was issued. Appellant then filed a second petition for PCRA and an application for extraordinary relief to stay the warrant of execution. The stay was granted pending the trial court's determination as to whether appellant suffered from a mental illness which would prevent him from comprehending the reasons for the death penalty. The trial court found appellant competent and again denied his request for PCRA relief. Upon review, the court held that the claims asserted had been previously litigated on direct appeal and affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied appellant's petition for post conviction relief because the claims had previously been litigated on direct appeal and were therefore not appropriate for post conviction relief. The court also affirmed the trial court's decision that found appellant competent to be executed.

 

55 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Parsonese v. Midland Nat'l Ins. Co.


No. 64 E.D. Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


550 Pa. 423; 706 A.2d 814; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 60


October 20, 1997, Argued  
January 20, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County entered on July 17, 1996 at No. 94-05896-19-1. JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Honorable Susan D. Scott.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, contingent beneficiaries of a life insurance policy, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the primary beneficiary, enforced the life insurance contract without its modification by 20 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6111.2, and entered judgment awarding the proceeds of the policy to appellee.


OVERVIEW: A decedent's life insurance policy named his ex-wife, appellee, as primary beneficiary and his children from previous marriages, appellants, as contingent beneficiaries. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee and awarded her the proceeds. The trial court declined to apply 20 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6111.2 and enforced the contract without modification by the statute because it found that retroactive application of § 6111.2 would violate the contract clauses, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Pa. Const. art. I, § 17. The court affirmed, holding that although the contracts clauses protected contracts from subsequent legislative impairment, they did not prohibit a state from exercising its police power, even if it altered contracts. The court found that because § 6111.2 severely impaired the insurance contract by eliminating the decedent's designation, the statute required careful scrutiny. The court then applied a five-factor test and found that § 6111.2, as applied to this case, would be unconstitutional, in violation of the contract clause. The court also held that that the remedy was to refuse to apply the statute retroactively to avoid the constitutional conflict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of the life insurance proceeds to appellee, primary beneficiary, and against appellants, contingent beneficiaries, because the retroactive application of the statute unconstitutionally violated the contracts clauses of the United States and Pennsylvania constitutions because it severely impaired the beneficiary designation in the contract and was not necessary to safeguard any vital interest of the people.

 

56 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cass


No. 12 Western District Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


551 Pa. 25; 709 A.2d 350; 1998 Pa. LEXIS 8


September 18, 1996, Argued  
January 7, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 29, 1998. Certiorari Denied October 5, 1998, Reported at: 525 U.S. 833, 142 L. Ed. 2d 70, 119 S. Ct. 89, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5077.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania dated October 4, 1995 at No. 2134 PGH 1994, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division dated November 18, 1994 at No. 1690 of 1994. 466 Pa. Super. 66, 666 A.2d 313.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Superior Court reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania that affirmed the trial court, which held that reasonable suspicion and not probable cause was required before school officials could conduct a search of appellee student's locker. The court held that the search did not meet the reasonable suspicion standard and suppressed the drugs found in the student's locker.


OVERVIEW: During a general search of all the lockers at the student's high school, drugs and drug paraphernalia were found in the student's locker. The student was arrested and charged with possession of marijuana and possession of drug paraphernalia and moved to have the seized items suppressed. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court and held that the search conducted was properly conducted under both U.S. Const. amend. IV and Pa. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held that the privacy interests of the student were limited and gave the student no greater protection under the Pennsylvania Constitution than under the United States Constitution. The court held that the search of the student's locker under both the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions required only reasonable suspicion and given all the circumstances present at the inception of the search, it was reasonable because it was minimally intrusive and affected a limited privacy interest of the student. The search was compatible with the Pennsylvania Constitution because it was carried out based upon neutral, clearly articulated guidelines.


OUTCOME: The order of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded back to the trial court. The student's motion to suppress was denied because under both the United States and Pennsylvania Constitutions, the search required only reasonable suspicion and the search was reasonable because it was minimally intrusive and affected a limited privacy interest.

Commonwealth v. Gribble


No. 72 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


550 Pa. 62; 703 A.2d 426; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2523


January 23, 1996, Argued  
November 20, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Reargument Denied March 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Pa. LEXIS 208. Certiorari Denied November 16, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 7341.
Reargument denied by Commonwealth v. Gribble, 1998 Pa. LEXIS 208 (Pa., Mar. 2, 1998)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Commonwealth v. Gribble, 580 Pa. 647, 863 A.2d 455, 2004 Pa. LEXIS 3135 (2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Gribble v. Folino, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 105724 (E.D. Pa., Nov. 10, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at, Sub nomine at O'Donnell v. Lamas, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 185868 (E.D. Pa., Jan. 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of Death, Entered on August 11, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Trial Division, at 92-12-2081-2092. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Paul Ribner.



DISPOSITION: The verdict and sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of, inter alia, first degree murder, criminal conspiracy, and robbery, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2502(a), 903, and 3701, and imposed the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of, inter alia, first degree murder, criminal conspiracy, and robbery, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2502(a), 903, and 3701, and from the imposition of the death sentence. The court affirmed. Defendant's smashing the victim's head with a hammer supported a finding of specific intent to kill, and circumstantial evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant and co-defendant killed the victim in the course of a robbery. Defendant waived his claim that the trial court failed to suppress evidence as he withdrew his pre-trial motion to suppress under Pa. R. Crim. P. 323. Regardless, his arrest and the search were legal as the dwelling owner consented to the search. The Commonwealth did not violate the disclosure requirements of Pa. R. Crim. P. 305(B)(1)(b), as it did not possess the crossed-out portion of defendant's confession, even though such was in police custody. The automatic proportionality review of mitigating and aggravating circumstances in death penalty cases under Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9711(h) was properly conducted, as the data upon which the court relied afforded defendant protection from arbitrariness and anomalies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of, inter alia, first degree murder, criminal conspiracy, robbery, and abuse of a corpse because the evidence was sufficient to establish specific intent, defendant waived his claim to evidence suppression, and the Commonwealth complied with disclosure requirements. The court affirmed the death sentence after conducting the statutory proportionality review.

Commonwealth v. Stern


No. 43 E.D. Appeal Docket 1995, No. 44 E.D. Appeal Docket 1995, No. 45 E.D. Appeal Docket 1995


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


549 Pa. 505; 701 A.2d 568; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2332


December 9, 1996, Argued  
October 30, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, Entered June 12, 1995, at Nos. 9500-2665, 9500-2662 and 9500-2636.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Philadelphia County Court of Common Pleas is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which upheld a municipal court's determination that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4117(b)(1), was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine by infringing on the sole authority of the judiciary to regulate the conduct of members of the legal profession.


OVERVIEW: The lower courts agreed with defendant attorneys that the statute they were charged with violating, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4117(b)(1), was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine. On appeal, the state argued that the doctrine was not offended by a statute that criminalizes conduct of an attorney for compensating a non-lawyer for client referrals because the legislature has the power to classify crimes. The court pointed out that Rule 7.2(c) of the Rules of Professional Conduct prohibited an attorney from giving anything of value to a person for recommending the attorney's services, except for payments of advertising or charges imposed by referral services or legal service organizations, and that § 4117(b)(1) was essentially a restatement of Rule 7.2(c). The court found that the effect of § 4117(b)(1) was to criminalize the conduct of attorneys and noted that the law did not establish a duty imposed uniformly upon citizens to forego payments to individuals for business or client referrals. The court held that the statute specifically acted to regulate attorneys, which infringed on the judiciary's sole authority to regulate attorney conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower courts' judgment that the statute that defendants were accused of violating was unconstitutional. The court noted that prohibiting attorneys from paying for referrals was part of the exclusive authority granted by the state constitution to the judiciary to supervise the conduct of attorneys. The court held, therefore, that the challenged statute was unconstitutional because it infringed upon that authority.

Commonwealth v. Mulholland


No. 65 W.D. Miscellaneous Docket 1997, No. 67 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997, No. 66 W.D. Miscellaneous Docket 1997, No. 66 W.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


549 Pa. 634; 702 A.2d 1027; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2102


September 16, 1997, Argued  
October 10, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, allowed by grant of this court's extraordinary jurisdiction entered on July 31, 1997, and transferred sua sponte by order of the Superior Court at Nos. 1060 and 1170 PGH 1997 on August 8, 1997, from the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, entered on April 22, 1997, at No. CC-9600418. JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Honorable David R. Cashman.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's order insofar as it held that double jeopardy does not act as a bar to reprosecution is affirmed. With respect to all other issues, those raised by the Commonwealth, the order is reversed, and the case is remanded for retrial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Commonwealth sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), holding that double jeopardy did not bar reprosecution of respondents for involuntary manslaughter after prosecutorial misconduct, that selective prosecution did bar retrial, that venue or venire could not be relitigated, and that the district attorney was to be removed from prosecution.


OVERVIEW: During the trial of respondent police officers for involuntary manslaughter, a witness commented on their privilege under U.S. Const. amend. V, and the trial court declared a mistrial. The trial court ordered that double jeopardy did not bar reprosecution, that selective prosecution did bar retrial, that venue or venire could not be relitigated, and that the district attorney was to be removed from prosecution and replaced by the attorney general. On appeal, the court affirmed the order on the issue of double jeopardy, holding that none of the examples of prosecutorial misconduct, individually or in combination, established a prosecutorial intent to deprive respondents of a fair trial to the extent that would bar retrial. The court held that the trial court erred in its decision that selective prosecution was a bar to reprosecution since there was no evidence of impermissible reasons to select respondents for prosecution. Since the question of venire was not one determinative of the law of the case, it could be relitigated in the trial court in which the complaint was originally filed. The trial court erred in removing the district attorney from prosecution sua sponte.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order holding that double jeopardy did not bar reprosecution despite prosecutorial misconduct but reversed those portions holding that retrial was barred due to selective prosecution, that venire could not be relitigated, and that removed the district attorney from prosecution and substituted the attorney general. The case was remanded.

Commonwealth v. Morales


No. 84 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


549 Pa. 400; 701 A.2d 516; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1920


November 8, 1995, Submitted  
September 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied November 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, dated December 8, 1994, denying appellant's second petition for post-conviction relief from the judgment of sentence entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County at Nos. 1292-1295, October Term 1982.

JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Albert F. Sabo (C.P.).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) denying defendant's second petition pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9551.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, following a jury trial, of first degree murder, criminal conspiracy, and possession of an instrument of crime. Following a penalty proceeding, the jury sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed the trial court's order denying his second petition for post conviction relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9541-9551. On appeal, the court reversed the order and remanded for a new sentence hearing, holding that remarks during the prosecutor's closing argument to the jury at defendant's penalty hearing constituted reversible error. The court held that generally comments by a prosecutor do not constitute reversible error unless the unavoidable effect of such comments would be to prejudice the jury, forming in their minds fixed bias and hostility toward the defendant so that they could not weigh the evidence objectively and render a true verdict. The court further held that, in this case, the prosecutor's remarks exceeded his authority because they implied that defendant should get the death penalty because otherwise he would be joining the ranks of defendants who have been wrongly released from jail by liberal judges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that denied defendant's second petition for post conviction relief and remanded for a new sentence hearing, holding that remarks during the prosecutor's closing argument to the jury at defendant's penalty hearing constituted reversible error.

Brinkley v. King


No. 15 W.D. Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


549 Pa. 241; 701 A.2d 176; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1902


September 19, 1996, Argued  
September 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court dated October 18, 1995, at No. 0594PGH95, affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division, dated January 25, 1995, at No. 939 of 1993 D.R. 448 Pa. Super. 646, 671 A.2d 765 (1995).

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania entered October 18, 1995, at No. 0594PGH95, which affirmed the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division, entered January 25, 1995 at No. 939 of 1993 D.R. 448 Pa.Super. 646, 671 A.2d 765 (1995).

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court Entered October 18, 1995, at No. 594 Pittsburgh 1995, Affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division, Entered January 25, 1995, at No. 939 of 1993 D.R. 448 Pa. Super. 646, 671 A.2d 765 (1995).

Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court of Pennsylvania entered October 18, 1995, at No. 0594PGH95, which affirmed the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division, entered January 25, 1995 at No. 939 of 1993 D.R. 448 Pa.Super. 646, 671 A.2d 765 (1995).



DISPOSITION: The order of Superior Court is vacated and the case is remanded to the trial court [***2] for a hearing on the issue of estoppel.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pennsylvania denying her motion for adjudication of paternity in her action against appellee father for child support.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother was married to her husband at the time when her daughter was conceived, but appellant was also having an affair with appellee father. After the child was born, appellant filed an action against appellee, claiming that the support that appellee paid was insufficient. Appellee denied paternity and refused to take a blood test. Appellant filed a motion for adjudication of paternity. The lower court denied her motion, holding that she had not presented clear and convincing evidence that her husband had no access to her during the period of conception. On appeal, the court vacated and remanded, finding that the presumption of the husband's paternity had no application to the case because the purpose of the presumption, to protect the institution of marriage, could not be fulfilled. At the time of appellant's complaint for support, there was no marriage. Appellant and her husband separated before the birth of the child and were divorced at the time of the complaint. Accordingly, the court held that it was error for the lower court to fail to consider the estoppel evidence because estoppel evidence could be presented if the presumption did not apply.


OUTCOME: The order denying appellant mother's motion for adjudication of paternity in her action against appellee father for child support was vacated and remanded. The court found that the presumption of appellant's husband's paternity had no application to the case because the purpose of the presumption, to protect the institution of marriage, could not be fulfilled. At the time of appellant's complaint for support, there was no marriage.

Stuski v. Lauer


No. 31 M.D. Appeal Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


548 Pa. 338; 697 A.2d 235; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1195


April 16, 1997, SUBMITTED  
June 17, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Direct appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court Entered April 4, 1997 at No. 0268 M.D. 1997. JUDGE(S) BELOW: - / Commonwealth - Hon. Joseph T. Doyle.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate filed a pro se direct appeal of an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee individual's petition to set aside appellant's nomination petition to appear on the May 20, 1997, primary ballot as a Democratic candidate for Justice of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court granted appellee individual's petition to set aside appellant candidate's nomination petition to appear on the May 20, 1997, primary ballot as a democratic candidate for Justice of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania, appellant challenged. In affirming, the court held that the trial court correctly set aside appellant's nomination petition because appellant failed to have 100 signatures on her nomination petition from Monroe County, as was required by 25 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2872.1(8). Furthermore, the trial court properly struck 20 signatures from appellant's nomination petition for failing to meet statutory requirements because 14 signatures were not from registered democratic voters in Monroe County, one signature was printed, and five signatures did not provide the signer's occupation, residence, and date of signing. The court further held that appellant waived her claim that the statutory requirements of 25 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2869, which required a signer to provide his occupation, residence, and date of signature, were unconstitutional because appellant failed to raise the issue below.


OUTCOME: The court issued a per curiam order denying appellant candidate's pro se direct appeal and affirming the order of the trial court, which set aside appellant's nomination to appear on the primary ballot as a democratic candidate for Justice of the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania, because appellant failed to obtain 100 signatures from Monroe County, as was statutorily required.

Allen by Allen v. Montgomery Hosp.


Nos. 36 Eastern Appeal Docket 1996 & 37 Eastern Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


548 Pa. 299; 696 A.2d 1175; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1182


October 17, 1996, ARGUED  
June 17, 1997, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6918.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court dated December 19, 1995 at No. 3129 Phila. 94, reversing the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Civil Division at 83-16964. JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Honorable William T. Nicholas / SUPERIOR - MCEWEN, JOHNSON, BROSKY, JJ.

Appeal from the Judgment of the Superior Court entered on December 19, 1995 at 3129PHL94 reversing the order entered on August 18, 1994 and remanding to the Court of Common Pleas, Montgomery County, Civil Division at 83-16964. 447 Pa. Super. 158, 668 A.2d 565 (1995). JUDGE(S) BELOW: CCP - Honorable William T. Nicholas / SUPERIOR - MCEWEN, JOHNSON, BROSKY, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and reinstated the trial court in favor of appellants on the verdict of the jury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, hospital and doctor, sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) reversing the order of the trial court holding appellants immune from liability under the Mental Health Procedures Act, 50 P.S. § 7114 and remanding the matter for a new trial, in an action for medical negligence.


OVERVIEW: Appellee parents' daughter (patient) was admitted to a psychiatric hospital for treatment of mental illness. Patient was later transferred to appellant hospital for treatment of physical ailments pursuant to an agreement between the two hospitals. While undergoing treatment patient was kept in a vest restraint. The patient accidentally hanged herself in the restraint while attempting to get out of bed, causing her to suffer permanent brain damage. Appellees filed a suit against appellants, hospital and doctor, for medical negligence. Appellants claimed immunity under the Mental Health Procedures Act (MHPA), 50 P.S. § 7114. A jury returned a verdict in favor of appellants pursuant to the MHPA after finding that neither appellant had been grossly negligent in the treatment of the patient. The superior court reversed and remanded the matter for a new trial holding that the immunity provisions of the MHPA did not apply. On appeal, the state supreme court reversed the superior court's decision holding that the MHPA granted appellants limited immunity for undertaking the treatment of the mentally ill patient for physical ailments pursuant to a contract with the psychiatric hospital.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court reversing the trial court's order to hold appellants, hospital and doctor, immune from liability in a medical negligence action filed by appellee parents was reversed and the trial court's order was reinstated. The immunity provision of the Mental Health Procedures Act applied to a hospital and a doctor providing medical care for physical ailments to mental patient pursuant to a contract with a mental hospital.

Torbik v. Luzerne County


No. 0196 M.D. Miscellaneous Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


548 Pa. 230; 696 A.2d 1141; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1192


March 19, 1997, SUBMITTED  
June 17, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order entered June 28, 1996, in the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County at No. 2972-C of 1996. JUDGES: Hon. Mark A. Ciavarella, Jr.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hotel owners challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), holding that the Third Class County Convention Center Authority Act, 16 Pa. Const. Stat. § 13101, et seq., and specifically, the Hotel Room Tax, 16 Pa Cons. Stat. § 13123, as well as Luzerne County, Pa. Ordinance 052296, were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Pennsylvania legislature adopted the Third Class County Convention Center Authority Act (Act), 16 Pa. Const. Stat. § 13101, et seq., which provided for the creation of authorities to own and operate convention centers. The Act included the Hotel Room Tax, 16 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 13123, which allowed counties where convention centers were located to impose a hotel rental tax, and, pursuant to this statute, Luzerne County passed Luzerne County, Pa. Ordinance 052296. Appellant hotel owners sought a declaration that the Act and the Ordinance were unconstitutional, but the trial court disagreed. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding specifically that the hotel room rental tax provision of the Act and the Ordinance passed pursuant to it were constitutional because the tax would not harm appellants and these were not prohibited special laws. The court found that the Luzerne County Convention Center Authority was properly incorporated and that the facility it was constructing did not violate the Municipal Authorities Act of 1945, 53 Pa. Const. Stat. § 306(A)(a), (b)(2) because the project differed from existing facilities and was the type of project envisioned by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order finding that the Third Class County Convention Center Authority Act, the Hotel Room Tax, and a Luzerne County ordinance were constitutional because they did not harm appellant hotel owners and were not special laws.

Bible v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 65 M.D. Appeal Docket 1995, No. 69 M.D. Appeal Docket 1995, No. 71 M.D. Appeal Docket 1995, No. 73 M.D. Appeal Docket 1995


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


548 Pa. 247; 696 A.2d 1149; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1141


March 5, 1996, ARGUED  
June 13, 1997, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Order of the Commonwealth Court dated August 4, 1995, at No. 77 M.D. 1995. 663 A.2d 837 (Pa. Cmwlth. 1995). JUDGES BELOW: Hon. James Gardner Colins, PJ.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and the case is remanded for entry of an order granting summary judgment in favor of the appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth challenged an order from the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee class of hearing impaired disability claimants after finding that 77 P.S. § 513(8) was unconstitutional insofar as it retroactively amended the Workers' Compensation Act, 77 P.S. § 1 et seq., regarding compensation for loss of hearing.


OVERVIEW: The Workers' Compensation Act, 77 P.S. § 1 et seq., was retroactively amended to change the benefits available to claimants with a hearing loss. Appellee class of hearing impaired disability claimants claimed that 77 P.S. § 513(8) was unconstitutional insofar as it retroactively changed the compensation for loss of hearing, and the trial court granted summary judgment in their favor. On appeal, the court reversed and ordered the trial court to enter summary judgment in favor of appellant commonwealth, holding that the retroactive application of the amendment was not unconstitutional. The court found that the retroactive application was a rational means to further a legitimate legislative purpose. Appellees had no vested right that attached at the time of their injury or at any time prior to an award of benefits. They had a recognizable interest in obtaining reasonable compensation for employment related injuries, not a right to compensation of a fixed amount. The court concluded that appellees' right to receive compensation for hearing loss had not been impaired, only the remedy had been varied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee class of hearing impaired disability claimants because the retroactive application of an amendment to the Workers' Compensation Act that changed the compensation for loss of hearing was not unconstitutional. The court ordered the trial court to enter summary judgment in favor of appellant commonwealth.

Cherry v. City of Phila.


No. 96 E.D. Appeal Docket 1994


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


547 Pa. 679; 692 A.2d 1082; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 814


February 28, 1995, SUBMITTED  
April 23, 1997, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Commonwealth Court Entered November 24, 1993, at No. 579 C.D. 1993, Affirming the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, Entered February 2, 1993, at No. 467 November Term 1992 160 Pa. Cmwlth. 179, 634 A.2d 754 (1993). JUDGES BELOW: Honorable Bernard J. Avellino (C.C.P.). Pellegrini, Kelley, Lord, JJ., (Cmwlth).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of an order of the Commonwealth Court (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his declaratory judgment action that challenged the constitutionality of appellee city's imposition of certain business taxes and licensing requirements upon him for practicing law in the city.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney practiced in one city but made court appearances in appellee city. Appellee notified appellant that he was in violation of provisions of the local code that required non-residents to pay tax on profits earned from doing business in the city. The code also required persons that did business in the city to obtain a business privilege license. Appellant did not obtain a license or pay taxes. Upon receipt of notice from appellee, appellant filed a declaratory judgment action, alleging that the local code provisions were unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint because appellant failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The lower court affirmed. On appeal, the court found that the city code provided a process for appeal of determinations of tax liability. The court held that because appellee only sent a notice, there had been no determination of tax due. Appellant had not exhausted his administrative remedies. The court held that the local code provisions did not infringe on the court's ability to regulate the practice of law because the provisions imposed interest, fines, and criminal penalties but did not prevent appellant from practicing law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed appellant attorney's declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of local business tax and license provisions because appellant failed to exhaust administrative remedies. The court also found that appellee city's imposition of business taxes and licensing requirements on appellant did not infringe on the court's constitutional authority to regulate the practice of law.

Commonwealth v. Bronshtein


No. 88 Capital Appeal Docket


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


547 Pa. 460; 691 A.2d 907; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 590


December 6, 1995, ARGUED  
March 25, 1997, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 20, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6380.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Ott, J.), Criminal Division, No. 3279-93, dated August 10, 1994. JUDGE BELOW: Hon. Stanley R. Ott.



DISPOSITION: The verdict and sentence of death imposed upon appellant by the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence of death in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), for his convictions of first degree murder, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2502(a); robbery, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3701; theft of movable property, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3921(a); possession of an instrument of crime, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 907; and criminal conspiracy to commit murder, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his death sentence. On appeal, the court held that there was ample evidence to sustain defendant's conviction. Defendant's statements to the police were admissible because he voluntarily waived his Miranda rights and because his right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. IV had not attached to this charge. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in precluding the requested voir dire question because another question was used to elicit the same information. The commonwealth's exclusion of a prospective juror was not violative of the law because there were proper reasons for excluding that juror. The trial court did not err in allowing defendant's statement that he had killed another man for the limited purpose of establishing the identity of the murderer in this case. A witness's testimony that defendant told him he killed someone was not vague and thus, was admissible. The exclusion of testimony about another murder was not error because defendant had not established a logical connection between that murder and his alleged crimes. The trial court did not err in refusing to grant a mistrial. The sentence imposed was based upon the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence in the trial court because the evidence was sufficient to support his convictions. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in determining the admissibility of evidence, defendant's constitutional rights were not violated, the prosecutor did not commit misconduct, and the sentence was based on the evidence.

Commonwealth v. Stewart


No. 24 M.D. Appeal Docket 1995


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


547 Pa. 277; 690 A.2d 195; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 425


January 23, 1996, ARGUED  
February 24, 1997, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court Order No. 1853 PHILA 1991 entered August 2, 1994, affirming Columbia County Court of Common Pleas Order No. 339 of 1990 Term entered May 16, 1991. 436 Pa. Super. 262, 647 A.2d 597. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Gailey C. Keller, P.J. (C.C.P.) BECK, POPOVICH, HOFFMAN, JJ. (SUPERIOR)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant catholic church challenged the judgment of the Superior Court (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the order of the trial court that required appellant to produce documents to the trial court for an in camera review in a murder case where self defense, based upon a priest's past behavior, was alleged by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, and in preparation of his defense, defendant subpoenaed documents from appellant catholic church. The trial court ordered appellant to produce the documents, and the intermediate appellate court affirmed. Appellant challenged the order, contending that production of the documents violated the clergy-communicant privilege and its U.S. Const. amend. I right to the free exercise of religion. The court affirmed, holding that application of the clergy-communicant privilege was not based solely on the clergy's status, but whether the communication was made in confidence in the context of a penitential or spiritual matter. Since the information requested only regarded the manner in which the appellant conducted its affairs, the court held that the clergy-communicant privilege did not apply. The court further held that the appellant's U.S. Const. amend. I rights were not violated because the production of the documents furthered a compelling governmental interest by the least restrictive means available and did not impermissibly intrude upon appellant's exercise of its religious beliefs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that clergy-communicant privilege did not apply to documents kept in the course of appellant catholic church's business. The court further held that the required production of documents did not violate appellant's constitutional rights.

Commonwealth v. Baker


No. 4 Middle District Appeal Docket 1996


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


547 Pa. 214; 690 A.2d 164; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 334


September 18, 1996, ARGUED  
February 12, 1997, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Superior Court, entered August 11, 1995, at Docket No. 645 Harrisburg 1994 which affirmed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County, Criminal Division, entered August 24, 1994, at Docket No. 94-10, 220. 447 Pa. Super. 621, 668 A.2d 1186 (1995). JUDGE(S) BELOW: C.C.P. - Hon. John A. Walter / Superior - ROWLEY, P.J., WIEAND, KELLY, JJ.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the Superior Court is reversed. This case is remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. Jurisdiction is relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order from the Superior Court (Pennsylvania) that affirmed his in absentia conviction for driving under a suspended license under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1543(b). Appellant claimed that his failure to submit a self addressed stamped envelope with his motion for a continuance as required by the local rules did not relieve the clerk of court from its duty to notify him of his trial date under Pa. R. Crim. P. 9025.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, acting pro se, filed a motion to continue his trial on a charge of driving under a suspended license in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1543(b), but failed to comply with a local court rule requiring him to enclose a self addressed stamped envelope (SASE) with the motion. Therefore, the clerk of courts did not send appellant a copy of the order resetting the trial date, appellant did not appear at trial, the trial court convicted appellant as charged in absentia, and the appellate court affirmed the conviction. On appeal, the court held that because the determination of appellant's guilt occurred after the effective date of revised Pa. R. Crim. P. 9025, which imposed a mandatory duty on the clerk of courts to send copies of the trial court's orders to all parties or attorneys, and because the local rules could not void a mandatory duty, appellant was entitled to receive a copy of the court's order setting his trial date regardless of whether or not he submitted an SASE pursuant to the local rules. Therefore, the court reversed the order and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's in absentia conviction for driving under a suspended license and remanded the case. The court held that because state procedural rules required the clerk of courts to send appellant copies of the trial court's orders, appellant was entitled to received notice of his rescheduled trial date although he did not comply with a local rule to send a self addressed stamped envelope with his motion for a continuance.

In re Assignment of Avellino


No. 2 Eastern District Miscellaneous Docket 1997


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge from the court of common pleas challenged orders from the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania, in an action to direct the petitioner to show cause why he should not comply with his official judicial assignment and to comply with the assignment given him by the administrative judge.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner judge from the common pleas court refused to comply with an official assignment by the administrative judge of the trial division of that court. A rule from the court directed the petitioner to show cause why he should not comply with the assignment, and the judge was ordered to comply with the assignment pending further order from the supreme court. Petitioner's refusal to comply with the order of the court constituted defiance of legitimate authority. The court issued orders for the filing of an application for disqualification, and for the petitioner to appear and show cause why he should not be sanctioned.


OUTCOME: The court ordered petitioner judge to appear and show cause why he should not be sanctioned, and also ordered the filing of an application for disqualification, because the supreme court had jurisdiction over the matter, and the petitioner had no right or interest to receive or continue in any assignment or type of assignment.

Pennsylvania State Police v. Hospitality Invs.


No. 77 Eastern District Appeal Docket 1992


SUPREME COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


547 Pa. 142; 689 A.2d 213; 1997 Pa. LEXIS 304


July 8, 1996, SUBMITTED  
February 6, 1997, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Entered at No. 9104-3255, Civil Division on July 23. 1991. JUDGES BELOW: Hon. Bernard J. Avellino.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state liquor board challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that held that Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-498, which barred appellee liquor licensee from advertising liquor prices, violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 7. The court reversed, finding the statute was valid under U.S. Const. amend. XXI, but the U.S. Supreme court remanded the case for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state liquor board fined appellee liquor licensee for advertising the prices of its liquor drinks in violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 47, § 4-498. However, the trial court ruled that § 4-498 violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 7. The court reversed the order, finding that § 4-498 was a valid exercise of the commonwealth's right to regulate liquor under U.S. Const. amend. XXI. The U.S. Supreme Court remanded the case for reconsideration after the U.S. Supreme Court decided a similar case from another state. The court held that the U.S. Supreme Court ruled that U.S. Const. amend. XXI did not qualify the prohibition against laws abridging free speed in U.S. Const. amend. I. The court held that U.S. Const. amend. I set the minimum levels applicable to Pa. Const. art. I, § 7, and that the court was bound to follow the decision of the U.S. Supreme Court with respect to its interpretation of the U.S. Constitution. Therefore, because the U.S. Supreme court invalidated a similar statute from another state as an impermissible infringement on free speech, § 4-498 violated the U.S. and Pennsylvania constitutions. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order finding that the law barring appellee liquor licensee from advertising its liquor prices, violated the state constitution. The court held that it was bound to follow the U.S. Supreme Court's ruling that liquor regulations could not abridge the right of free speech under the U.S. Constitution and that the federal constitution set the minimum standards that applied to analogous state constitutional provisions.
