Cairns v. Cairns


No. 1217 EDA 1999


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1999 PA Super 281; 741 A.2d 800; 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4037


September 30, 1999, Argued  
November 19, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Family Division, No. 009415817. Before ZALESKI, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Family Division (Pennsylvania), denying his petition to transfer venue of a child support order entered by an Oregon court to Pennsylvania in favor of appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it ruled that the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act (UIFSA), 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 7101-7901 was not an unconstitutional denial of appellant's due process rights. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of Oregon's application of the provisions of the UIFSA, which permitted Oregon to exercise personal jurisdiction over him in order to establish a child support order. There was no evidence to suggest that appellant was denied the ability to seek review of Oregon's Circuit Court decision that it had personal jurisdiction over him. Appellant filed subsequent motions regarding the order and there was no evidence he preserved a personal jurisdiction challenge. The appropriate manner in which to challenge the validity of the statute was by direct appeal to the Oregon Court of Appeals.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed; appellant was precluded from collaterally attacking the issues of personal jurisdiction and the constitutionality of the Oregon statute in Pennsylvania and, therefore, the denial of his petition to transfer venue was appropriate.

 

197 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Heidler


No. 1096 Harrisburg 1997


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1999 PA Super 266; 741 A.2d 213; 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3965


September 8, 1999, Argued  
November 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied April 18, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 946.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence October 14, 1997, Docketed October 17, 1997, In the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County Criminal Division at No. 96-2043. Before BAYLEY, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed Appellant's judgment of sentence dated October 14, 1997, and remanded this case to the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County for entry of an order discharging Appellant. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of possession of a weapon on school property, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 912(b), in the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County Criminal Division (Pennsylvania). Appellant claimed that the evidence did not support a finding that he had possession of his handgun.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his girlfriend went to pick up appellant's son from his school. Appellant gave his girlfriend his handgun, which she put in her purse. Appellant was found guilty of possession of a weapon on school property, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 912(b). Appellant claimed that there was insufficient evidence to find that he possessed the firearm on school property. Where appellant did not have access to the purse, appellant could not have been found to have had the necessary power to control or intent to control the gun. Trial judge could not have logically concluded, beyond a reasonable doubt, that appellant intended to exercise control over his handgun upon arriving at the school. Appellee Commonwealth did not meet its burden in proving the necessary element of possession. Judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: Reversed. Trial judge could not have logically concluded, beyond a reasonable doubt, that appellant intended to exercise control over his handgun upon arriving at the school. Appellee Commonwealth did not meet its burden in proving the necessary element of possession.

 

198 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Brown


No. 73 Harrisburg 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1999 PA Super 257; 741 A.2d 726; 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3453



October 19, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised November 10, 1999. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied November 20, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 2507.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, September 24, 1997, In the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal, Nos. 318 and 320 CD 1997.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated. Remanded for resentencing. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) contending the Registration of Sexual Offenders Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791 - 9799.6 violated his right to due process by requiring him to rebut the statutory presumption that he was a sexually violent predator.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a violent repeat sex offender who preyed upon the frailties of defenseless elderly women. The court held that the trial court properly determined that 25 to 50 years imprisonment was insufficient to protect the public safety. The court found that sufficient reasons were placed on the record for imposition of the first life sentence. However, the trial judge did not provide sufficient justification on the record as to the reasons a second life sentence would be necessary. The court held that the Registration of Sexual Offenders Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 9791 - 9799.6 governing the registration of sexual offenders, commonly known as "Megan's Law", which imposed the presumption that an individual who had been convicted of an enumerated offense was a sexually violent predator and required an individual to rebut such presumption by clear and convincing evidence, violated the individual's right to due process of law.


OUTCOME: Judgment of sentence vacated and remanded for resentencing holding Megan's Law, imposing the presumption that an individual who had been convicted of an enumerated offense was a sexually violent predator and required an individual to rebut such presumption by clear and convincing evidence, violated the individual's right to due process.

 

199 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Spierling v. First Am. Home Health Servs.


No. 1441 Pittsburgh, 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1999 PA Super 222; 737 A.2d 1250; 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2819; 16 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 308


April 21, 1999, Argued  
September 1, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Dismissed September 24, 1999. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 1894.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of July 13, 1998, In the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County, Civil Division, at No. GD98-8104. Before FOLINO, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), granting appellees' preliminary objections and dismissing appellant's wrongful termination complaint.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee sued appellees, her former employer and its successor corporation, for wrongful discharge and age discrimination. Appellant claimed she was fired for reporting suspected Medicare fraud by appellee employer, based on her review of old and discarded files. The trial court granted appellees' preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer and dismissed the complaint. Appellant challenged only the dismissal of her wrongful discharge claim, and the court affirmed. Since appellant did not demonstrate that she was under a statutory duty to search the files for evidence of Medicare fraud and report the alleged fraud to federal investigators, she was not entitled to relief on public policy considerations from the at-will employment doctrine.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the complaint was affirmed. Because appellant was under no statutorily imposed duty to report suspected past Medicare fraud by appellee employer, appellees were within their rights to discharge her as an at-will employee for making such reports.

 

200 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Downing


No. 34 Pittsburgh 1998


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1999 PA Super 216; 739 A.2d 169; 1999 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2782


February 22, 1999, Submitted  
August 24, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered December 4, 1997, in the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County, Criminal No. CA 1682 of 1995. Before HANCHER, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, with a blood alcohol content of 0.145 percent 71 minutes after his automobile accident, filed an appeal from the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of driving under the influence in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3731(a)(1) and (a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was involved in an accident and arrested after failing three field sobriety tests. Seventy-one minutes after the accident, he was given a test, which revealed a blood alcohol content (BAC) of 0.145 percent. He was charged with DUI pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3731(a)(1) and (a)(4) and a jury found him guilty. The court affirmed conviction, rejecting appellant's argument that the trial court should not have permitted evidence of his BAC to support the charge under Section 3731(a)(4) because the commonwealth did not present expert relation-back testimony. Once the commonwealth established that appellant's BAC reflected an amount above 0.10 percent, the commonwealth made a prima facie case and it was not required to present expert testimony relating the BAC test result back to the time appellant was driving. Because appellant did not present any evidence that might have rebutted the commonwealth's prima facie case, his conviction under Section 3731(a)(4) was proper. The evidence was sufficient to sustain his conviction under Section 3731(a)(1), including a trooper's observations of appellant, the results of three field sobriety tests, and appellant's BAC.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, holding that once the commonwealth established that appellant's BAC was above 0.10 percent, it made a prima facie case and was not required to present expert testimony relating the test result back to the time that appellant was driving. The evidence was sufficient to sustain his conviction.
